[<p><em>Welcome to \u201cInside the Green Room with Danny Green,\u201d a Yahoo Sports podcast and video series hosted by Toronto Raptors forward Danny Green and Harrison Sanford.\xa0</em></p>, <p>Danny talks about what it\u2019s like to return to San Antonio as a visiting player after spending the last eight seasons there.</p>, <p>Danny talks about what he did on\xa0 New Year\u2019s Eve and <p>Danny and Rudy talk about what it will be like to face off against their former teams and how players on both sides approach a regular-season game that gets this much hype.</p>, <p>Danny and Rudy talk about the prediction DeMar DeRozan made during the summer on Serge Ibaka\u2019s cooking show and how these games can go one of two ways for the players in the spotlight.</p>, <p>Danny and Rudy [<p>In the end, the biggest match of the Premier League season so far more than lived up to the billing. Because not only was <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:Manchester City" href="/soccer/teams/manchester-city/">Manchester City</a>\u2019s pulsating, back-and-forth 2-1 win over table-topping <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:Liverpool" href="/soccer/teams/liverpool/">Liverpool</a> an instant classic; not only was it the Reds\u2019 first loss of the campaign; it also sets up a dramatic end to the best title race in recent memory, with more than four months of matches still to play.</p>, <p>It\u2019s hard to imagine any of those games topping this one.</p>, <p>When England\u2019s best two teams last met in October, <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:it was a dud;outcm:mb_qualified_link;_E:mb_qualified_link" href="https://sports.yahoo.com/unfortunately-neutral-fans-manchester-city-liverpool-pretty-much-punchless-183413788.html">it was a dud</a>. Liverpool and City were even on points then, and in retrospect it shouldn\u2019t have been surprising that what was always going to be a cagey contest ended scoreless.</p>, <p>The stakes were significantly higher on Thursday. The Reds entered the match at the Etihad leading City by a whopping seven points. That meant the home team would have to come out attacking, even if it meant risking punishment at the feet of the visitors\u2019 deadly counterattack.</p>, <p>That\u2019s how it played out when the whistle blew, too. But then Jurgen Klopp\u2019s team began to find their feet, and very nearly\xa0\u2014 oh, so nearly\xa0\u2014 the opening goal.</p>, <p>Instead, Sadio Mane hit the post after being played through by Mo Salah, and John Stones managed to clear what <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:would\u2019ve been a spectacular own-goal;outcm:mb_qualified_link;_E:mb_qualified_link" href="https://sports.yahoo.com/manchester-city-narrowly-avoided-embarrassing-goals-video-203047263.html">would\u2019ve been a spectacular own-goal</a> off the line in the 18th minute:</p>, <p>In real time, it looked as though the ball was in. Referee\xa0<span>Anthony Taylor immediately looked at his watch for a signal from the electronic eye-in-the-sky that it had indeed crossed the line. None came, and they played on. Moments later, the millions of fans watching from every corner of the globe learned just how close the call actually was:\xa0</span></p>, <p>I mean\u2026 <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:pic.twitter.com/nW2ZRAEfHQ" href="https://t.co/nW2ZRAEfHQ" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">pic.twitter.com/nW2ZRAEfHQ</a></p>, <p>\u2014 NBC Sports Soccer (@NBCSportsSoccer) <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:January 3, 2019" href="https://twitter.com/NBCSportsSoccer/status/1080923354582958080?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">January 3, 2019</a></p>, <p><br/></p>, <p>Mane had another chance to put the visitors ahead against reeling City moments later. But after his volley was squandered, Pep Guardiola\u2019s men seemed to regain their composure. And they took a 1-0 lead into the dressing room at halftime thanks to a brilliant individual goal by Sergio Aguero five minutes before the break.</p>, <p>When the second stanza began, the hosts appeared fully in control. But yet again, Liverpool willed its way back into the tilt. And it managed to find an equalizer through Roberto Firmino off a well-worked sequence in the 65th minute to set up what would be an epic finish to the contest:</p>, <p>The momentum had clearly swung back toward Liverpool at that point. And with the Reds not content to sit back and protect the point (not to mention their lead in the standings), it was defending champion City who capitalized on a counterattack of their own, Leroy Sane firing home the strike that would stand up as the winner with about 20 minutes left to play:</p>, <p>Both teams now have 17 games remaining. Even though Liverpool\u2019s lead atop the table was cut to four, Klopp and Co. still controls their own destiny. The Prem crown is still theirs to lose.</p>, <p>\u201cThe boys tried everything, we got nothing for it. That\u2019s how it is sometimes in life,\u201d Klopp said afterward, adding that he felt City defender Vincent Kompany should\u2019ve been sent off for a first-half foul on Salah. \u201c[If we] keep on going, everything will be fine for us.\u201d</p>, <p>Either way, things sure are a lot more interesting following a match that will surely go down as one of the greatest Premier League games ever played.</p>, <p><strong>More from Yahoo Sports:</strong><br/> <strong>\u2022 <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:Ticket prices plummet for college football title game;outcm:mb_qualified_link;_E:mb_qualified_link" href="https://sports.yahoo.com/title-game-ticket-prices-plummeting-90-percent-college-football-worried-214530894.html">Ticket prices plummet for college football title game</a><br/> \u2022 <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:Steelers\u2019 Brown responds to ex-teammate, calls him \u2018Uncle Tom\u2019;outcm:mb_qualified_link;_E:mb_qualified_link" href="https://sports.yahoo.com/antonio-brown-responds-ex-teammate-ryan-clark-calling-uncle-tom-022147795.html">Steelers\u2019 Brown responds to ex-teammate, calls him \u2018Uncle Tom\u2019</a><br/> \u2022 <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:Soaring TV ratings, streaming viewership an NFL bright spot;outcm:mb_qualified_link;_E:mb_qualified_link" href="https://sports.yahoo.com/nfl-television-ratings-2018-games-five-percent-streaming-viewership-soars-211117632.html">Soaring TV ratings, streaming viewership an NFL bright spot</a><br/> \u2022 <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:Thamel: How Saban\u2019s evolution changed Alabama;outcm:mb_qualified_link;_E:mb_qualified_link" href="https://sports.yahoo.com/open-scoring-nick-sabans-evolution-changed-alabama-025126292.html">Thamel: How Saban\u2019s evolution changed Alabama</a><br/> </strong></p>]

That was 13 days ago (Dec. 22). They will finish their road trip on Saturday at Houston in their American Athletic Conference opener.</p><p>Baylor, meanwhile, ended a 16-day break on New Year's Eve with a 98-37 victory over Texas Rio Grand Valley. The Bears are 9-1, their lone loss coming on Dec. 15 at No. 11 Stanford, 68-63.</p><p>UConn is 4-2 all-time against Baylor, including a 72-61 win over the Bears in their last meeting on Nov. 17, 2016, when Baylor was ranked No. 2 nationally and the Huskies No. 3.</p><p>The Huskies have also won 126 straight regular season games and 58 consecutive non-conference games, two marks that should be tested by the Bears, who have one of the nation's best \u2014 and tallest \u2014 frontcourts in 6-foot-7 center Kalani Brown (14.8 points, 6.8 rebounds per game) and 6-4 forward Lauren Cox (11.7 points, 6.4 rebounds).</p><p>UConn's tallest starter is 6-3 Katie Lou Samuelson, although coach Geno Auriemma has inexperienced 6-4 freshman Oliva Nelson-Ododa available off the bench.</p><p>"You really can't," Auriemma told the Connecticut Post about preparing for that type of size in practice. "As much as you think you might be able to, you can't. There's very little way that you can simulate how they play and how big they are and how physical they are.</p><p>"You just have to go down and play the game and try to figure out different ways defensively that you can try to negate some of that."</p><p>One way for UConn to combat Baylor's size is to push the tempo, something the Huskies are\xa0comfortable doing, led by veteran point guard Crystal Dangerfield, Samuelson and emerging freshman guard Christyn Williams. Senior forward Napheesa Collier, who averages 18.6 points and a team-high 10.5 rebounds, will also provide matchup problems for the Bears' frontcourt with her speed and ability to get down the court in transition.</p><p>"They do have a lot of bigs and they don't like to run as much," Collier told the Post. "Obviously, transition's one of our strong suits. We're going to try to run a lot."</p><p>Samuelson continues to lead the Huskies in scoring (20.1) while Dangerfield (13.8), Williams (13.8) and sophomore Megan Walker (10.8) also average double figures.</p></p>, <p>UConn's top-ranked women's basketball team resumes its four-game road trip after another extended break when it visits No. 8 Baylor on Thursday at the Ferrell Center in Waco, Texas.</p>, <p>The nationally-televised game (ESPN) is set to tip at 9 p.m.</p>, <p>The last time we saw the Huskies (11-0) they were completing the first two legs of their journey with a 76-66 victory over previously unbeaten and No. 14 California in Berkeley. [<p>Ernesto Valverde\u2019s contract expires in six months\u2019 time but the FC Barcelona coach is only focused on defending the La Liga title.</p>, <p>His team are facing a mean Getafe on Sunday, while Sevilla host Atletico Madrid, as the\xa0La Liga leaders look to reach the halfway point of the season.</p>, <p>They need a win at miserly Getafe to take another step towards retaining the title.</p>, <p>Valverde, whose contract expires in June, says he is determined to triumph and is not distracted by anything else.</p>, <p>\u201cWho knows?\u201d\xa0said Valverde on Tuesday when asked about his future by the club\u2019s own television channel. \u201cI\u2019m not thinking about the long or very long term. What I want is to win. I don\u2019t know what I\u2019ll be doing next year.\u201d</p>, <p><strong>READ ALSO</strong>:\xa0<a href="https://punchng.com/insecurity-police-deploy-more-units-in-katsina/"><span style="color: #ff0000;">Insecurity: Police deploy more units in Katsina</span></a></p>, <p>FC Barcelona has dominated in Spain over the past decade, winning seven of the last 10 titles, and are three points clear at the top of La Liga after 17 matches.</p>, <p>Although team captain Lionel Messi stated at the start of the season that the club\u2019s aim was to win the UEFA Champions League, domestic success appears crucial to that goal.</p>, <p>Nobody will begrudge them that desire, after seeing rivals Real Madrid win the trophy three years running.</p>, <p>FC Barcelona, who have won the European Cup five times, have only ever done so while also triumphing in the Spanish top-flight.</p>, <p>They head to the Coliseum Alfonso Perez on Sunday looking to start 2019 in style, with Lionel Messi and Luis Suarez back after an\xa0extended winter break.</p>, <p>They will be aiming to unpick the league\u2019s second tightest defence.</p>, <p>Getafe received good news in that regard\xa0this week with Djene Dakoman, their key defender, fit again after a foot injury.</p>, <p>The Togo centre-back has been a crucial part of the backline, with Getafe conceding just 13 goals in the opening 17 matches \u2014 only Atletico have conceded fewer with 12.</p>, <p>Last season Getafe became the first team to stop FC Barcelona from scoring in a dour 0-0 draw at Camp Nou.</p>, <p>That same defensive solidity has lifted the Madrid side to seventh place.</p>, <p>However midfielder Gaku Shibasaki, who scored a brilliant volley against FC Barcelona in September 2017, will be missing after being called up by Japan to compete in the Asian Cup.</p>, <p>European champions Real Madrid host Real Sociedad on Sunday, with the visitors hoping the new year, brings a change in fortunes after a disappointing 2018.</p>, <p>The Basque side, who are 15th, sacked coach Asier Garitano on Boxing Day and his replacement, Imanol Alguacil, is excited about the challenge ahead.</p>, <p>\u201cSurely there is no better place to start (than the Santiago Bernabeu),\u201d\xa0said Alguacil.</p>, <p>\u201cWe visit an amazing stadium and play against an amazing team, and we will go there as we always do, going out to play, which is to say, trying to take the three points.\u201d</p>, <p>Earlier on Sunday, third-placed Sevilla will host second-placed Atletico Madrid, with Diego Simeone\u2019s visitors able to pull level on 37 points with leaders FC Barcelona before they kick off at Getafe.</p>, <p>Uruguayan defender Jose Maria Gimenez returns from injury for Atletico Madrid, although Lucas Hernandez and Filipe Luis are poised to miss the game, along with striker Diego Costa.</p>, <p>Sevilla will be missing attacking midfielder Franco Vazquez after he was sent off for dissent in the clash with Leganes on Dec. 23.</p>, <p>The Andalusians had rescued a draw from that game in stoppage time.</p>, <p>The weekend\u2019s other fixtures include Levante vs Girona, Espanyol vs Leganes and Real Valladolid vs Rayo [<p>LAS VEGAS, NEVADA - NOVEMBER 23: Nassir Little #5 of the North Carolina Tar Heels dunks against Kris Wilkes #13 of the UCLA Bruins during the 2018 Continental Tire Las Vegas Invitational basketball tournament at the Orleans Arena on November 23, 2018 in Las Vegas, Nevada. (Photo by Sam Wasson/Getty Images)</p>, <p class="speakable-content">The <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/11/27/personal-nba-top-50-according-san-antonio-spurs-values/">San Antonio Spurs</a> have been on a tear as of late, but they could still be in a position to nab a high-flying freshman out of Chapel Hill in Nassir Little. Bleacher Report\u2019s <a href="https://bleacherreport.com/articles/2811588-final-2019-nba-mock-draft-before-the-new-year#slide0">Jonathan Wasserman</a> compiled his last mock draft of 2018, in which he had Little slotted as being the 13th pick in the first round of the <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/12/18/san-antonio-spurs-early-2019-nba-draft-prospects-jarrett-culver/">2019 NBA Draft</a>.</p>, <p class="speakable-content">Despite being in the same recruiting class as the likes of <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/11/17/san-antonio-spurs-tank-zion-williamson/">Zion Williamson</a> and R.J. Barrett, it was Little who garnered the preseason accolades, being named the MVP and Co-MVP of the McDonald\u2019s All-American Game and Jordan Brand Classic respectively. Such a feat placed Little in rarified air, <a href="https://bleacherreport.com/articles/2811408-nassir-little-is-learning-the-hard-way">joining LeBron James as the only other to win MVP honors in both events.</a></p>, <p>Little, once considered a near-lock as a top-three pick coming into the season, has seen his draft stock drop off precipitously during his time playing in the Dean Dome.\xa0 Let\u2019s investigate how his game would translate to the Spurs system if\xa0San Antonio had the opportunity to select Little.</p>, <p>The 6\u20196\u2033 forward is currently averaging 10.8 points on 51.5 percent shooting and 4.2 rebounds in just 19.4 minutes of play over his first 12 collegiate games. On the surface, these numbers pale in comparison to that of players such as Williamson and Barrett.\xa0 Further, Little has connected on just five three-pointers all year on 21.7 percent shooting from downtown.</p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">It just hit me. Nassir Little's freshman year REALLY reminds me of Vince Carter's.</p>, <p>Vince played 18 minutes per game and averaged 7.5 points.</p>, <p>Nassir is playing 19 minutes per game and averaging 10.8 points.</p>, <p>Both showed flashes of brilliance &amp; both looked a bit lost at times too</p>, <p>\u2014 nbabeau (@NBABeau) <a href="https://twitter.com/NBABeau/status/1079070951067795456?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">December 29, 2018</a></p>, <p><script async="" charset="utf-8" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></p>, <p>Seeing the raw numbers will undoubtedly create a healthy level of skepticism about Little\u2019s transition to the next level. However, there are several other factors at play that have prevented Little from producing in the same eye-popping manner UNC fans saw prior to his arrival on campus.</p>, <p>Little is joining a senior-laden Tar Heel roster, which has forced the freshman to adopt a bench role and that adjustment has resulted in a productivity drop-off as he transitions to the college game. Despite his early season fluctuations, Little\u2019s start to his freshman season is eerily similar to that of another <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/07/18/san-antonio-spurs-danny-green-trade-instagram/">Carolina</a> legend: Vince Carter.</p>, <p>It\u2019s safe to say Carter\u2019s career turned out just fine as he\u2019s currently the oldest player in the NBA at the ripe young age of 41 with 21 years of league experience under his belt. While it\u2019s impossible and irresponsible to say Little\u2019s career will follow the same trajectory as Carter\u2019s, it shows that Little\u2019s slow start and the system he\u2019s playing in should not be an indictment on his ability to produce at the next level.</p>, <p>One of the greatest traits that Little possesses is one that cannot be taught: athleticism. When asked about the subject, UNC head coach Roy Williams said that <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P-ljTzoOXrY">Little is easily the most athletic player he\u2019s ever had the opportunity to coach</a>. With incredible explosion and leaping abilities, Little can glide through the lane and finish thunderous put back dunks.</p>, <p>Many teams and scouts will be enamored with Little\u2019s combination of size and speed, with the potential to develop into a two-way/3-and-D player if he\u2019s able to find a more consistent three-point shot. His strong 6\u20196\u2033, 220-pound frame coupled with his steady body control allows Little to absorb contact on drives and he has shown glimpses of instinctual positioning on the offensive glass for easy buckets.</p>, <p>While the physical traits are undeniable, Little has much room for growth on both ends of the floor to become a more well-rounded prospect. As mentioned, just the five three-point makes on the season at a low percentage is concerning. Further, Little has recorded just 10 assists this year (.08 APG), which is tied for seventh on the team and shows that he still has a ways to go as a facilitator and playmaker</p>, <p>As a fit for the <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/12/27/san-antonio-spurs-shouldve-sold-farm-luka-doncic/">Spurs</a>, Little is an ideal candidate. The two-way potential coincides perfectly with a team that\u2019s fundamentally rooted in defense. Plus, the addition of another explosive player to pair with the likes of a healthy <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/11/13/san-antonio-spurs-sorely-miss-dejounte-murray/">Dejounte Murray</a> and <a href="https://airalamo.com/2018/11/20/three-ways-lonnie-walker-can-jumpstart-san-antonio-spurs/">Lonnie Walker</a> would give Spurs fans a young and exciting core for years to come.</p>, <p>Currently, the Spurs\u2019 draft pick is hovering around the middle of the first round towards the back end of the lottery. While the Spurs do not traditionally trade up to acquire players.</p>, <p>If they believe Little is the piece they need they could consider packaging their two first round picks \u2013 including the Raptors first round pick they received from the <a href="https://www.basketball-reference.com/players/l/leonaka01.html" ref="nofollow">Kawhi Leonard</a> trade \u2013 to select Little.</p>, <p>Build your own custom daily newsletter with updates on your favorite teams, sent directly to your inbox.</p>, <p class="privacy" style="color: #000000">Your privacy is safe with us. We'll never pass along your email address to spammers, scammers, or the like.</p>, <p>Your favorite teams, topics, and players all on your favorite mobile devices.</p>, <p class="copyright">\xa9 2019 FanSided Inc. All Rights Reserved.</p>, <p class="byline author">by Noah Magaro-George</p>, <p class="byline author">by Kaelen Jones</p>, <p class="byline author">by Ethan Farina</p>, <p class="byline author">by Dylan Carter</p>]
[<p>West coast college basketball pits the Pacific Tigers against the Brigham Young Cougars.</p>, <p>The Brigham Young Cougars look to get in the win column after a 103-81 loss at Mississippi State saddled the team with a third straight loss.</p>, <p>Brigham Young trailed by ten after 20 minutes and never got their defense going with Mississippi State owning a 54.3%-43.3% shooting edge with ten more shots.</p>, <p>Yoeli Childs carried the Cougars with 25 points along with a team high six turnovers on 11-18 marksmanship with TJ Hawes adding 14 points, six rebounds and three steals on 4-15 from the floor and 5-5 at the stripe.</p>, <p>Zac Seljaas gave BYU 13 points, five pulls and three steals on 3-5 from the field and 6-6 at the stripe followed Luke Worthington and Jahshire Hardnett with eight points each.</p>, <p>The surging Pacific Tigers have won five of six after downing UC Irvine 84-73 in overtime as a 3.5 point home dog.</p>, <p>Pacific was outshot 44.4%-41.9% but turned 34 Anteaters fouls in to a 33-19 advantage at the charity stripe which was decisive.</p>, <p>Ajare Sanni topped the Tigers offense with 23 points on 8-16 accuracy and 4-5 at the line followed Roberto Gallinat tossed in 20 points with five pulls on 2-8 shooting and 15-18 at the stripe.\xa0</p>, <p>Pacific received ten points and seven boards from Jahlil Tripp with Kendall Small tossing in nine points.</p>, <p>BYU are 1-8 ATS in their last 9 road games and over is 7-2 in BYU last 9 vs. West Coast and over is 9-3 in BYU last 12 overall. Pacific \xa0are 12-5-1 ATS in their last 18 vs. West Coast and Pacific are 12-5 ATS in their last 17 home games. BYU are 6-2 ATS in the last 8 meetings and favorite is 6-2 ATS in the last 8 meetings.</p>, <p>It\u2019s hard to compare these teams right now but Pacific is looking much improved\u2026</p>, <p class="article-author-date"><i class="fas fa-calendar"></i> <span content="2019-01-02T19:02:30-0500" itemprop="datePublished">1/02/2019 (EST) <i class="fas fa-sync"></i> <span content="2019-01-03T03:45:52-0500" itemprop="dateModified">1/03/2019 (EST)</span></span></p>, <p></p>, <p>Get the latest Sports News &amp; Picks.</p>, <p><iframe allow="autoplay" class="podcast" frameborder="no" height="450" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=https%3A//api.soundcloud.com/users/233867423&amp;color=%23ff5500&amp;auto_play=false&amp;hide_related=true&amp;show_comments=true&amp;show_user=true&amp;show_reposts=false&amp;show_teaser=true" width="100%"></iframe></p>, <p>Activities offered by advertising links to other sites may be deemed an illegal activity in certain jurisdictions. [<p>LOUDONVILLE \u2014 His first home game complete as Siena College men\u2019s basketball head coach, Jamion Christian credited the program\u2019s fans for the energy they had brought that evening to Times Union Center despite a losing effort from the Saints.</p>, <p>\u201cJust knowledgeable fans. They really have a great understanding of it,\u201d Christian said after that November game. \u201cIt\u2019s just a great feeling in the building, and you want to do a great job for [the fans] because they support us so well.\u201d</p>, <p>Then came the subtle ask, a gentle request for some patience \u2014 one of the few times Christian has done that since his May hire.</p>, <p>\u201cHopefully,\u201d Christian said, \u201cthey\u2019re pleased with our effort, and can kind of see where we\u2019re going with this thing and how it\u2019s going to build.\u201d</p>, <p>A little more than a month later, Siena provided an example of the on-court blueprint Christian is looking for his program to follow. In a <a href="https://dailygazette.com/article/2018/12/29/siena-men-s-basketball-finishes-2018-with-blowout-win">21-point win against Cal Poly</a> to wrap their non-conference season, the <a href="https://dailygazette.com/article/2018/12/31/defense-stars-in-latest-siena-men-s-basketball-win">Saints\u2019 defense was stifling</a> and they used a 21-point advantage from behind the 3-point line to key their offense.</p>, <p>In short, the Saints had finally produced the \u201cMayhem\u201d Christian promised.</p>, <p>\u201cIt will look like that,\u201d Christian said afterwards. \u201cIt will be a great defensive \u2014 and connected \u2014 effort with our ability to make outside shots really impacting the game.\u201d</p>, <p>As MAAC play starts 4 p.m. Thursday for Siena at Saint Peter\u2019s, the question for the Saints is how repeatable the effort they delivered against Cal Poly is for them the rest of this season. Siena brings a 5-8 mark into conference play after a non-conference season during which the Saints mostly struggled to implement with success key parts of Christian\u2019s strategy, such as the team\u2019s full-court pressure defense.</p>, <p>\u201cI love pressing,\u201d Christian said in mid-December. \u201cWe just don\u2019t have the depth right now to do it consistently.\u201d</p>, <p>Siena has used its full-court press to slow opponents, but hasn\u2019t had much success turning over opponents. Partially, that is because too many current Saints lack the needed combination of height and foot speed \u2014 for most, the latter has been the larger issue \u2014 to make the press work. Looking ahead to next season, Christian said the infusion of incoming Saints \u2014 6-foot-6 Shawn Walker, 6-foot-8 Luke Sutherland and 6-foot-10 Kyle Young \u2014 should help Siena address that issue.</p>, <p>\u201cI love size. Here, I think I can get size and athleticism,\u201d Christian said. \u201cSo I think we\u2019re going to be able to [press] better down the road, but we need to do a good job with it right now, too.\u201d</p>, <p>When Christian coached at Mount St. Mary\u2019s for six seasons, he often had to choose between athleticism and size when bringing in a player. Routinely, he took on long-term projects in need of serious development \u2014 and if a player\u2019s potential was realized, he often soon transferred to a stronger league than the Northeast Conference, which is simply part of life for NEC coaches.</p>, <p>Meanwhile, at Siena, Christian expressed confidence within his first few weeks on the job that he could attract \u201chigh-level transfers.\u201d That confidence has already been rewarded, as Siena added redshirt junior Elijah Burns \u2014 a Troy native who started his college career at Notre Dame \u2014 to its program earlier this season. With a smile, Christian said last month he wasn\u2019t surprised his coaching staff was able to bring an ACC-level talent into the fold during its first season at Siena.</p>, <p>\u201cI never believe in setting any limits,\u201d said Christian, whose program is still waiting to find out if Burns will be declared eligible to play the rest of this season.</p>, <p>And despite Siena sitting three games below .500 and the <a href="https://dailygazette.com/article/2018/12/20/limitations-show-in-siena-men-s-basketball-loss">limitations of this season\u2019s roster</a>, there is little reason to put a cap on this season\u2019s potential for the Saints within MAAC play. In the 11-team league, seven teams registered between three and five wins during the non-conference season \u2014 and only one program, Niagara, heads into MAAC play with a winning record. All that is certain about Siena\u2019s future is that the last-place prediction MAAC coaches placed upon the Saints before the season started will only be met if Siena underperforms during the next couple months, which Christian\u2019s squad heads into off its best team performance of the season and with a pair of its players \u2014 senior Evan Fisher and freshman Jalen Pickett \u2014 reigning as the league\u2019s top player and rookie of the week.</p>, <p>The future remains a bright one for Siena, but the immediate future appears brighter than was expected months ago.</p>, <p>\u201cI think we\u2019ve got a chance to be pretty special,\u201d said Christian, whose Mount St. Mary\u2019s teams went a combined 67-39 in league play. \u201cI think we\u2019ve just got to continue to grow.\u201d</p>, <p><em>Reach Michael Kelly at <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#2845434d444451684c494144514f49524d5c5c4d06464d5c"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="e68b8d838a8a9fa682878f8a9f81879c83929283c8888392">[email\xa0protected]</span></a> or <a href="https://twitter.com/ByMichaelKelly">@ByMichaelKelly</a> on Twitter.</em></p>]

Bale went down, <strong>but it soon became clear the foul wasn't the direct cause of his distress, with the Real Madrid man holding his left calf.</strong></p>, <p>Having been attended to by the Real Madrid medical team on the touchline, Bale came back onto the pitch in the 40th minute, but he was <strong>clearly limping and struggled to break into a run during the remainder of the first half. [<p>Welcome to NHL.com, the official site of the National Hockey League</p>, <p>Bienvenue \xe0 LNH.com , le site officiel de la Ligue nationale de hockey</p>, <p>\u0414\u043e\u0431\u0440\u043e \u043f\u043e\u0436\u0430\u043b\u043e\u0432\u0430\u0442\u044c \u043d\u0430 NHL.com, \u043e\u0444\u0438\u0446\u0438\u0430\u043b\u044c\u043d\u044b\u0439 \u0441\u0430\u0439\u0442 \u041d\u0430\u0446\u0438\u043e\u043d\u0430\u043b\u044c\u043d\u043e\u0439 \u0445\u043e\u043a\u043a\u0435\u0439\u043d\u043e\u0439 \u043b\u0438\u0433\u0438</p>, <p>Tervetuloa NHL:n viralliselle nettisivustolle NHL.comiin</p>, <p>V\xe4lkommen till NHL.com, NHL:s officiella web-sida</p>, <p>V\xedtejte na NHL.com, ofici\xe1ln\xedch str\xe1nk\xe1ch National Hockey League</p>, <p>Vitajte na NHL.com, ofici\xe1lnych str\xe1nkach National Hockey League</p>, <p>Willkommen auf NHL.com, der offiziellen Seite der National Hockey League</p>, <p><b>BUFFALO --</b> <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-23E0A69D3ACDF50ECD69A">Jack Eichel</span> will miss at least the next two games for the Buffalo Sabres because of an upper-body injury.</p>, <p>The 22-year-old center will not play games against the Florida Panthers at KeyBank Center on Thursday (7 p.m. ET; MSG-B, FS-F, NHL.TV) or at the Boston Bruins on Saturday. The Buffalo captain, who sustained the injury in the first period of a 3-1 loss to the New York Islanders on Monday, will be re-evaluated next week.</p>, <p>"Obviously, Jack's a big part of our team," Sabres coach Phil Housley said. "It's a day-to-day situation, which is really encouraging. But we want to be cautious with it as well. There's a lot of hockey to be played."</p>, <p>Eichel, named to the NHL All-Star Game on Wednesday, leads Buffalo with 49 points (15 goals, 34 assists) in 40 games this season. He has 30 points (11 goals, 19 assists) in the 23 games since his line with <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-475C61E09E67048049C83">Jeff Skinner</span> and <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-E29502A399FF12689A285">Sam Reinhart</span> first began playing together Nov. 13. The Sabres have gone 12-7-4 during that stretch; at least one of the three has scored in all but four of those games.</p>, <p>"There's an opportunity there," Skinner said. "Everyone in here plays in the NHL so it's a good challenge for us. Obviously, it's a big hole to fill but we're going to try to fill it by committee."</p>, <p>Forward <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-76B53D0EC4D11E6398785">Evan Rodrigues</span> will get the first crack at filling in on the top line. A Boston University alumnus like Eichel, he knows he doesn't have to change much on his end.</p>, <p>"They're two highly skilled players who have had a great season so far," Rodrigues said of Skinner and Reinhart. "I'm just going to play my game, let them play theirs and just try to get them the puck as much as possible."</p>, <p>Housley rotated the top center spot after Eichel left the game Monday. Rodrigues' versatility earned him the chance to get the call against the Panthers.</p>, <p>Rodrigues has 11 points (two goals, nine assists) in 34 games this season.</p>, <p>"[Rodrigues] has been used in a lot of different capacities -- power play, penalty kill, moving up and down the lineup. That's what he brings to our team," Housley said. "The next stage is just his contributions offensively and trying to finish and go to the net hard. He's doing all the right things right now. Hopefully that translates into production."</p>, <p class="modal-share-text"></p>, <p class="btm-nhl-announcement-modal__body text--sans-serif-display">\n                    The NHL uses cookies, web beacons, and other similar technologies. [<p></p>, <p><span class="s1">Yves Leterme, the chief investigator of UEFA's Club Financial Control Body, has said <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/manchester-city">Manchester City</a> may be banned from the Champions League if they are found to have breached financial\xa0fair play (FFP) regulations.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">An investigation into allegations that City circumvented cash flow in order to get around FFP rules is ongoing, and Leterme told Belgian publication <em>Sport and Strategy</em> (h/t <a href="https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/uefa-chief-confirms-manchester-city-could-be-banned-from-champions-league-5ml5q7083?utm_medium=Social&amp;utm_source=Twitter#Echobox=1546535234" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Martyn Ziegler</a> of the<em> Times</em>) that if they are found guilty of any wrongdoing, the sanctions will be severe:</span></p>, <p><span class="s1"><em>"If it is true what has been written, there might be a serious problem. This can lead to the heaviest punishment: exclusion from the UEFA competitions.</em></span></p>, <p><span class="s1"><em>"If the information is correct, this possibly goes against truthful reporting. The FFP rules are based on a system of declaration, three months after the clubs have closed their accounts, they have to deposit their figures. Then we do random checks on the truthfulness of those figures. The accounts are examined and approved internally and externally."</em></span></p>, <p></p>, <p><span class="s1">As Ziegler relayed, German magazine<span>\xa0</span><em>Der<span>\xa0</span>Spiegel</em><span>\xa0</span>passed on allegations from Football Leaks that City's owners\u2014the<span>\xa0</span>Abu<span>\xa0</span>Dhabi<span>\xa0</span>United Group\u2014paid\xa0<span>\xa359.2 million</span><span>\xa0</span>to the club; the money was reported to have come from sponsors<span>\xa0</span>Etihad<span>\xa0</span>initially.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">The club, according to a number of leaked emails, are also said to have backdated sponsorship deals.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">If City have misreported the income, then it would be a breach of<span>\xa0</span>FFP<span>\xa0</span>rules and would seemingly result in significant ramifications for the Manchester outfit.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">In Ziegler's report, it's noted the Premier League team have been punished for breaches previously, as they were hit with an initial \xa349 million fine in 2014; it's added that amount was reduced to \xa316 million after City complied with stipulations put in place by UEFA's governing body.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">Per<span>\xa0</span><a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/football/2019/01/03/uefa-chief-investigator-confirms-manchester-city-could-face/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><span class="s2">Tom Morgan</span></a><span>\xa0</span>of the<span>\xa0</span><em>Daily Telegraph</em>, in the past City said "the attempt to damage the club's reputation is organised and clear" in regards to the most recent allegations. As such, the Premier League champions said they would not be offering any comment on the matter.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">The quotes from<span>\xa0</span>Leterme<span>\xa0</span>emerged ahead of City's crucial clash with Liverpool in English football's top flight on Thursday.</span></p>, <p><span class="s1">Ahead of the game, City trailed the Reds by seven points after a challenging festive period.\xa0Jurgen<span>\xa0</span>Klopp's Liverpool side head to the<span>\xa0</span>Etihad<span>\xa0</span>Stadium having won 17 and drawn three of their 20 Premier League games so far.</span><em>\xa0</em></p>]

However, the Rockets have completely turned things around, and they're doing it with <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/players/playerpage/555969/chris-paul">Chris Paul</a> out of the lineup. Houston has been victorious in 10 of its last 11 games, including its current five-game winning streak.</p>, <p>The <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/teams/GS/golden-state-warriors/">Golden State Warriors</a> also haven't had the start that many envisioned coming off their second consecutive NBA title. <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/players/playerpage/1685204/stephen-curry">Stephen Curry</a> missed time earlier this season due to a groin injury and <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/players/playerpage/1755178/demarcus-cousins">DeMarcus Cousins</a> has yet to debut with Golden State after signing with the team in the offseason. The Warriors have won back-to-back games -- against the <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/teams/POR/portland-trail-blazers/">Portland Trail Blazers</a> and <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/teams/PHO/phoenix-suns/">Phoenix Suns</a> -- and will be looking to continue to build momentum as 2019 begins.</p>, <p>While both teams will likely look quite different when the postseason rolls around, this certainly could be a playoff preview.</p>, <p>Check\xa0<a href="http://www.sportsline.com/nba/picksheet/#link=%7B%22role%22:%22standard%22,%22href%22:%22http://www.sportsline.com/nba/picksheet/%22,%22target%22:%22_blank%22,%22absolute%22:%22%22,%22linkText%22:%22Sportsline's%20NBA%20pick%20sheet%22%7D" target="_blank">Sportsline's NBA pick sheet</a>\xa0for all your daily odds.</p>, <p><strong>Rockets</strong>: Since Paul suffered a hamstring strain last month, there's been one driving force for the Rockets and it's been <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/players/playerpage/1685255/james-harden">James Harden</a>. Harden is playing the best basketball of his NBA career, and that's really saying something considering he's coming off an MVP Award. Over the past five games, he's averaging 41.8 points and shooting 41.5 percent from beyond the arc. If the Rockets want to top the defending champions, they're going to need another stellar effort from Harden.</p>, <p><strong>Warriors</strong>: It's been an up-and-down season for the Warriors to say the least. However, one of the biggest issues has been the shooting struggles of <a href="https://www.cbssports.com/nba/players/playerpage/1647559/klay-thompson">Klay Thompson</a> to this point. Thompson is currently averaging 21.0 points while shooting 34.4 percent from beyond the arc. While those are solid numbers, Thompson is a 41.6 percent shooter from 3 over the course of his NBA career.\xa0</p>, <p>Both teams were expected to be at the top of the Western Conference once again this season. The Rockets didn't get off to the best start, but are really hitting their stride now. At full strength, Houston could give Golden State all it could handle, but the Warriors will prove to be too much in this one.</p>, <p class="Newsletter-checkbox">\n<label class="CheckButton CheckButton-newsletter" data-checkbox-expanded-options='{"checkboxId":"CheckButton-checkbox","tableIds":""}' data-component="checkboxExpanded"><input class="CheckButton-checkbox" id="CheckButton-checkbox" name="check" type="checkbox"/><span class="CheckButton-checkmark CheckButton-newsletter"></span><span class="CheckButtonText">I agree that CBS Sports can send me the "CBS Sports HQ Daily Newsletter" newsletter.</span></label>\n</p>, <p class="site-footer-dates">\xa9 2004-2019 CBS Interactive. [<p style="color: #878787; font-size: 13px;">\n                      by <a href="/news/correspondents/sean-fitzpatrick.php">Sean Fitzpatrick</a> | <a href="/nba/team-news.php?team=TOR">Raptors Correspondent</a> | <span>Thu, Jan 3rd 6:51pm EST</span> </p>, <p style="font-size:14px; clear: both;">\n                        Kyle Lowry has been ruled out for Thursday's game versus the Spurs with a back injury. Lowry will now miss his sixth game in the past eight contests. Freddie Van Vleet will start again in his place. (<a href="https://twitter.com/JLew1050/status/1080970391718375424https://twitter.com/JLew1050/status/1080970391718375424" target="_blank">Josh Lewenberg on Twitter</a>)                    </p>, <p><b>Fantasy Impact:</b></p>, <p>With Lowry out again, Van Vleet remains a solid option in DFS while also being a solid streamer in season-long leagues. Kawhi Leonard will exact a lot of revenge tonight so he's a must-start in daily.</p>, <p style="color: #878787; position: relative;"><small>Category: \n<a href="/nba/injury-news.php">Injury Updates</a></small> | \n<small>More Kyle Lowry: </small></p>, <p class="copyright">\xa9 Copyright 2010-2019 FantasyPros.com</p>]
[<p class="article-summary"></p>, <p><p>If you and your buddies roll the ball in the fairway, take a mulligan per side, give each other 6-foot downhill putts and have only a casual acquaintance with lateral hazards vs. out-of-bounds shots, there\u2019s probably not much you need to know about the changes to the Rules of Golf for 2019.</p><p>Then again, some of the stuff you\u2019ve been getting away with in your circle of friends might now be permissible \u2014 so read on.</p><p>When Jan. 1, 2019 dawned, it was a new era in golf for those who play by the strict rules. The big news is that the word strict has a new meaning.</p><p>\u201cThe rules are more player-friendly,\u201d said Tom Dudley, a Jacksonville resident and veteran United States Golf Association rules official.</p><p>Do you have a 20-foot downhill putt from the back of the green to a front pin? You can leave the flag in the hole to take some of the sting out if the ball kisses the stick.</p><p>Did you accidentally hit the ball while taking practice putting strokes? It won\u2019t cost you as dearly as before.</p><p>Were you afraid that taking a drop in the rough would result in a lie buried under several inches of Bermuda grass? That drop, required from arm\u2019s length in the past, is now a matter of a few inches.</p><p>On the other hand, you get two minutes less to find a lost ball. But your playing partners will love it.</p><p>Those are just some of the changes to the rules of golf that took effect at the stroke of midnight of the new year.</p><p>The USGA and the Royal and Ancient Golf Club, which jointly administer the rules, made the most sweeping changes to how the game is conducted since eliminating stymies. The intent is to make the rules less complicated and archaic, so as to not drive away players \u2014 bad for business.</p><p>\u201cI think we\u2019re seeing the USGA and R&amp;A go more with a more common-sense approach to the rules,\u201d said Deerwood Country Club director of golf and Northern Chapter PGA president Tim Cooper. \u201cThey seem to have decided that just because a rule has always been this way is not sufficient reason to mean it has to stay that way.\u201d</p><p>Many of the rules also have to do with reducing the amount of time it takes to play a round of golf \u2014 one of the most frequent reasons players who leave the game cite.</p><p>For starters, the number of rules has been reduced from 34 to 24. There are sections and sub-paragraphs in all of them but the current Rules of Golf book has only 180 pages devoted to the rules.</p><p>The purists aren\u2019t all that happy and wonder why golf has to be dumbed down. But from an economic standpoint, golf can\u2019t survive being played only by the purists.</p><p>Those who want to peruse the changes in detail need only visit usga.org. But here are the highlights:</p><p>\u2022 Players are allowed to putt with the flagstick in the hole. No need to have a playing partner tend the flag, which will save time.</p><p>"I think a lot of handicap players will like this rule," Cooper said.</p><p>The pros are already in different camps as far as leaving the flag in the hole.</p><p>Bryson DeChambeau has said he will leave the pin in, even on short putts. Justin Thomas said he will never do it.</p><p>"I wouldn't be able to take myself seriously," Thomas told the Associated Press. "I just feel like it would be very, very weird."</p><p>\u2022 Clubs and tournaments can adopt a local rule to eliminate the stroke-and-distance penalty for shots hit out of bounds or lost balls. The drop also can take place at the nearest point in the fairway (no closer to the hole), with a two-stroke penalty, eliminating the two-club-length rule. Professional and elite amateur events will not use this rule modification.</p><p>\u2022 Drops will be made from knee height, not from the arm outstretched, even with a player\u2019s shoulder.</p><p>\u2022 There will not be a stroke penalty for a double-hit. If the ball strikes the clubface twice during one stroke, players only have to count the two strokes.</p><p>\u2022 If a player accidentally moves the ball on the green, it can be replaced at the nearest point with no penalty. Also, if a player accidentally marks a ball a fraction of an inch off, such as the 2017 incident involving Lexi Thompson, the penalties won't be nearly as severe if officials judge that the player made an honest mistake.</p><p>\u2022 Spike marks can be repaired on the green in your putting line. Players also can touch the line of their putt with no penalty.</p><p>While most of the rules have the potential to speed up play, repairing spike marks might not be one of them, at least on the pro level.</p><p>Tapping down any imperfections on your putting line ... I think some people might get carried away with that," Rory McIlroy told AP.</p><p>\u2022 Players can remove loose impediments in bunkers and hazards, such as leaves and rocks. You can also touch the ground or water in a hazard but still cannot ground the club behind the ball in a bunker.</p><p>\u2022 Players can actually avoid hitting out of bunkers at any time. They are allowed to drop outside bunkers, on a line between their ball and the green, no closer to the hole, with a two-stroke penalty.</p><p>\u2022 Only two modifications make current rules tougher. If you\u2019ve lost your ball, you get three minutes to find it, not five. Also, caddies cannot stand behind players and line them up for their shots.</p><p>Cooper said chatter from his members indicate their favorite changes are being able to remove debris from bunkers and hazards, drops from knee height and the reduced time being able to look for lost balls.</p><p>\u201cEveryone loves that new rule, except for the guy who lost the ball,\u201d Cooper said. \u201cBut they have studies that have shown that if you don\u2019t find the ball in three minutes, you\u2019re probably not going to find it within the additional two minutes.\u201d\xa0</p></p>, <p>If you and your buddies roll the ball in the fairway, take a mulligan per side, give each other 6-foot downhill putts and have only a casual acquaintance with lateral hazards vs. out-of-bounds shots, there\u2019s probably not much you need to know about the changes to the Rules of Golf for 2019.</p>, <p>Then again, some of the stuff you\u2019ve been getting away with in your circle of friends might now be permissible \u2014 so read on.</p>, <p>When Jan. 1, 2019 dawned, it was a new era in golf for those who play by the strict rules. You can leave the flag in the hole to take some of the sting out if the ball kisses the stick.</p>, <p>Did you accidentally hit the ball while taking practice putting strokes? It won\u2019t cost you as dearly as before.</p>, <p>Were you afraid that taking a drop in the rough would result in a lie buried under several inches of Bermuda grass? [<p>MEMPHIS, TN (WMC) - A former basketball player for the University of Memphis is now in custody after deputies asked for help tracking him down.</p>, <p><a href="http://www.wmcactionnews5.com/2019/01/02/former-uofm-basketball-player-accused-attacking-girlfriend-grocery-store/" target="_blank">Jimario Rivers</a>, 23, was wanted for aggravated assault. He\u2019s accused of attacking his girlfriend at Sprouts on Highway 64 last month.</p>, <p>Investigators say Rivers broke his girlfriend\u2019s cellphone and pulled her hair during an argument. The woman told police the last thing she remembered was waking up on the ground. Officers noted injuries to her face during her interview at the hospital.</p>, <p>On Dec. 28, Rivers was charged and an arrest warrant was issued.</p>, <p>Records show he was booked into jail Wednesday after deputies asked for help finding him. He\u2019s due in court Friday.</p>, <p>The Clarksville, Tennessee native played for the Tigers from 2016 to 2018.</p>, <p><i>Copyright 2019 WMC. The team did not comment on the report. Nightengale characterized the long-term offer as serious and likely closer to $200 million than $300 million, citing four people with knowledge of the offer who spoke on condition of anonymity. Nightengale also reported that Chicago has yet to make a formal offer for fellow premium free agent <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-0FB1A131B17AA84FE9894">Bryce Harper</span>, but remains in constant contact.</p>, <p>Machado visited the White Sox on the Monday following the Winter Meetings in Las Vegas. The team did not comment on the report. Nightengale characterized the long-term offer as serious and likely closer to $200 million than $300 million, citing four people with knowledge of the offer who spoke on condition of anonymity. Nightengale also reported that Chicago has yet to make a formal offer for fellow premium free agent <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-0FB1A131B17AA84FE9894">Bryce Harper</span>, but remains in constant contact.</p>, <p>Machado visited the White Sox on the Monday following the Winter Meetings in Las Vegas. He also made visits that week to the Yankees and Phillies who, like the White Sox, have expressed interest in both Harper and Machado.</p>, <p>According to Spotrac.com, the White Sox currently have $35,516,668 committed to their pre-arbitration payroll for 2019. In the midst of a rebuild, Chicago has the flexibility moving forward to sign Machado <i>and </i>Harper, although it's not certain if that situation will play out for any team.</p>, <p>Bringing in Machado as the team's third baseman would add to the infield mix featuring <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-477BC0469DD94655CCA9F">Tim Anderson</span> at shortstop and second baseman <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-0AA76483900AA10F6D2A3">Yoan Moncada</span>. <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-2C536809AE0828F35DA92">Jose Abreu</span> and recently acquired <span class="token token-playerCard" id="token-19AE5CB5327FA7EABDBAC">Yonder Alonso</span>, who is Machado's brother-in-law, will split time between first base and designated hitter. The White Sox are coming off a 100-loss season in 2018 but are selling Machado and Harper on the bright future with one of the best Minor League systems in the game and being able to become the face of the franchise.</p>, <p><a href="mailto:scott.merkin@mlb.com">Scott Merkin</a> has covered the White Sox for MLB.com since 2003. Follow him on Twitter <a href="http://twitter.com/@scottmerkin/">@scottmerkin</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/scottmerkinmlb/">Facebook</a> and listen to his <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/podcast/chicago-white-sox-podcast/id902521479?mt=2">podcast</a>.</p>]

[<p><strong>The four Boston first rounder could be more valuable than originally imagined</strong></p>, <p>As it stands right now the Boston Celtics would have four first round picks in the 2019 NBA Draft. Both teams would miss the Western Conference playoffs if the postseason started today despite both teams owning a .500 record, which is usually good enough to get you into the dance. Having two lottery picks has increased importance this year as the NBA is changing its lottery format for the first time in years. The Kings and Grizzlies are likely to finish with somewhere around the sixth to 14<sup>th</sup> worst records in the NBA. Under the old rules, teams in those slots would have virtually no shot at obtaining at top three pick. [<p class="wp-caption-text">SHANGHAI, CHINA - OCTOBER 26:  Brooks Koepka of the United States, and 2018 Caddy of the Year, Ricky Elliott, react a chip in on the 15th hole during the second round of the WGC - HSBC Champions at Sheshan International Golf Club on October 26, 2018 in Shanghai, China.  (Photo by Matthew Lewis/Getty Images)</p>, <p>11 hours ago</p>, <p>In what is the largest revision and modernization since 1984,\xa0the U.S. Golf Association implemented at least 31 major rules changes as of January 1.</p>, <p>Overall, the new rules were designed to make golf less intimidating and easier to understand as well as make the sport seem a bit more modern and speed it up a bit.</p>, <p>From\xa0allowing the flagstick to be left in the hole while putting on the green, to a new \u201cpace of play\u201d recommendation that suggests players make each stroke in no more than 40 seconds to eliminating a penalty if a player accidentally strikes the ball twice, the rules may take some getting used to, according to Southern Nevada Golf Association vice president and longtime rules official\xa0Sue May.</p>, <p>\u201cI am very enthused with the new rules, but it will be a process to get players educated because there are some significant changes,\u201d she told\xa0<em>The Las Vegas Review-Journal.</em>\xa0\u201cSome that are getting attention are players will now be able to ground the club in a penalty area, remove loose impediments in a penalty area, and the time to search for a lost ball has been reduced from five to three minutes.\u201d</p>, <p>As part of the update, the Players Edition rulebook is more intuitive and features simplified topical groupings, more direct language, and\xa0a \u201cpurpose of rule\u201d description section.</p>, <p>\u201cThey don\u2019t change rules just because it\u2019s going to make it difficult,\u201d <a href="https://www.pgatour.com/long-form/2019/01/01/biggest-rules-changes-golf-2019.html">said World Golf Hall of Famer Vijay Singh</a>. \u201cI think it\u2019s going to be easier. Major postseason projections have the Hoosiers safely in the NCAA tournament field, after a three-year hiatus.</p>, <p class="p-text">Closer to home, there appear to remain nagging doubts in the minds of some fans, begging a basic question: Is it safe to believe in this team yet? On current evidence, the answer ought to be a comfortable \u201cyes.\u201d</p>, <p class="p-text">Those close wins, coupled with Indiana\u2019s youth and worrisome injury problems, seem to be chief concerns for a fan base hopeful for an NCAA tournament return. If anything, though, it\u2019s the tight wins \u2014 and what Indiana learned from the experience \u2014 that ought to reassure them.</p>, <p class="p-text"><span class="exclude-from-newsgate"><strong>IU Insider</strong>: <a data-track-label="inline|intext|n/a" href="https://profile.indystar.com/newsletters/iu-insider/">Our email newsletter helps you keep up with the Hoosiers</a></span></p>, <p class="p-text"><span class="exclude-from-newsgate"><strong style="margin-right:3px;">More: </strong><a data-track-label="inline|intext|n/a" href="https://www.indystar.com/story/sports/college/indiana/2018/12/26/iu-basketball-midseason-report-romeo-langford-good-advertised/2400768002/">IU basketball midseason report: The good, bad and ugly from Hoosiers' hot start</a></span></p>, <p class="p-text">\u201cEverything that we've done to get here so far has been very, very hard-earned,\u201d Miller said Wednesday, \u201cWhether that's been tough, gritty wins, ugly play that's led to stellar, so to speak, defensive stops. We've had guys also step up and make timely baskets, and different people have stepped up at the end of the games. There's a lot of that good, blue-collar togetherness that has sort of been a part of what we've done.\u201d</p>, <p class="p-text">Miller wasn\u2019t defending IU\u2019s resume so much as explaining what his team got out of a difficult November and December, which didn\u2019t come without some lows.</p>, <p class="p-text">There were the last-second loss to Arkansas, the humbling defeat at Duke and those injuries, which appear to be as much of a concern in 2019 as they were in 2018.</p>, <p class="p-text">Miller said Wednesday during his first media briefing of the new year that redshirt senior guard Zach McRoberts could return from the back problem that held him out of the end of nonconference play. But freshman point guard Robert Phinisee is still in concussion protocol and hasn\u2019t practiced, with Miller saying IU will \u201cplan to move forward without him here for the foreseeable future.\u201d</p>, <p class="p-text">Long-term injury concerns Jerome Hunter (lower-body) and Race Thompson (concussion) likewise appear no closer to a conclusion.</p>, <p class="p-text">Those absences have opened doors for other Hoosiers. They\u2019ve handed freshman Damezi Anderson a bench role. Sophomore Al Durham has become a fixture in the starting lineup and among IU\u2019s ball handlers. And Devonte Green, who ended last season as Indiana\u2019s No. 1 point guard before beginning this one sidelined by his own injury, has begun to find his old form. He was the most recent recipient of IU\u2019s gold jersey, given to an outstanding practice performer.</p>, <p class="p-text">\u201cHe's done a nice job in practice leading into our last three wins. He's been a big, big part of our practices in term of him reengaging and being a primary player,\u201d Miller said. \u201cAs a coach, you worry about everything, but as a player, I think you see opportunity and you feel good that you're going to have a chance to contribute and be a part of this thing. I think that's pretty much what our guys have done (through injury problems). That's always how we have approached it, next man up, so to speak, and continue to work to get better and create an opportunity to change the path of your own individual season.\u201d</p>, <p>Indiana Hoosiers guard Devonte Green (11) is regaining his stride; here shooting against Jacksonville at Simon Skjodt Assembly Hall in Bloomington, Ind., on Dec. 22, 2018.<meta content="Bobby Goddin/For IndyStar" itemprop="copyrightHolder"/>\xa0<span class="credit">(Photo: Bobby Goddin/For IndyStar)</span></p>, <p class="p-text">None of that will automatically make January easier, much less successful.</p>, <p class="p-text">After the Illini leave Bloomington, IU must prepare for a weekend trip to conference frontrunner Michigan, then travel to Maryland at the end of next week. In total, the Hoosiers have to visit Michigan, Maryland, Michigan State and Purdue by Feb. 2, and their only two home games this month, after Illinois, are against the Wolverines and Nebraska.</p>, <p class="p-text">Ultimately, anyone wanting further evidence of this team\u2019s Big Ten and postseason credentials is about to get a heaping pile of it.</p>, <p class="p-text">The next month has the capacity to make or break Miller\u2019s team, and his second season in charge. The Big Ten is as strong as it\u2019s been in at least five years, maybe longer, and it\u2019s not prepared to wait for a young Indiana team to get back to 100 percent. It will also present the Hoosiers with chance after chance for resume-boosting wins, with this team already tight-game tested.</p>, <p class="p-text">\u201cWinning close games like that just builds toughness moving forward, being in those situations,\u201d grad transfer forward Evan Fitzner said. \u201cJust to have that experience moving forward will help us down the road in Big Ten and then hopefully in March.\u201d</p>, <p class="p-text">It will be March that matters most to this team, but January and February that decide whether it\u2019s worthy. Hanging onto at least some reservations about this group in the meantime is understandable. Just not at the expense of overlooking what the Hoosiers have proved about themselves already.</p>, <p class="p-text"><em>Follow IndyStar reporter Zach Osterman on Twitter: @ZachOsterman.</em></p>, <p class="p-text">\xa0</p>, <p class="p-text"><span class="print_infobox">7 p.m. Thursday</span></p>, <p class="p-text"><span class="print_infobox">TV: FS1</span></p>, <p class="p-text p-text-last" id="article-body-p-last">\xa0</p>]
[<p>By <b>Jamie Wall</b></p>, <p><i>Opinion - </i>It might have been on the back court in front of a couple of dozen fans, but the success of Paige Hourigan and her doubles partner Taylor Townsend is definitely worth talking about.</p>, <p class="photo-captioned__information">\n<span class="caption" itemprop="caption">Taylor Townsend and Paige Hourigan. </span>\n<span class="credit">Photo: <span itemprop="copyrightHolder">RNZ/SUPPLIED</span></span>\n</p>, <p>The women's game in New Zealand has lurched from bad to much worse in a year's time, so this ray of hope couldn't have come at a better time.</p>, <p>At last year's tournament, the only kiwi woman to make the main singles draw was Jade Lewis, who was comprehensively beaten by then-world number 138 Viktoria Kuzmova 6-4, 6-3.</p>, <p>Lewis, who received half a million dollars from private funding organisation The Seed Foundation, has since quit the sport to focus on her studies.</p>, <p>Just before Christmas, Marina Erakovic also announced she was pulling the pin on her career too.</p>, <p>Erakovic can look back on her time with some pride though, reaching a top singles ranking of 39 and being a feature on the WTA tour since 2005.</p>, <p>The best run she ever had at her home tournament was a losing doubles final in 2011.</p>, <p>The situation has become so dire that there was no New Zealand presence in the main singles draw at all, with Hourigan, Valentina Ivanov and Elys Ventura all failing to make it through qualifying.</p>, <p>After Lewis' disappointing showing, it was hard to blame tournament organisers for handing their three available wildcards to foreigners.</p>, <p>However, thanks to Hourigan and Townsend's inspired comeback, we're not just cut, pasting and slightly updating our articles from last year.</p>, <p>The duo prevailed 3-6, 6-1, 10-8 over Australian duo Monique Adamczak and Jessica Moore.</p>, <p>While neither of those two names will have tennis fans gasping in disbelief, it now means that there will at least be a kiwi presence on centre court at the business end of the tournament.</p>, <p>The magnitude of that is not lost on Hourigan.</p>, <p>"I'm super happy. [Taylor] is playing incredible, she's super solid and hopefully we can keep it going," the 21-year-old told us after the game.</p>, <p>"It's so easy for me to relax and play better when Taylor's there."</p>, <p>After dropping the first set, the pair struck back hard to blitz the Australians in the second. Hourigan found herself serving for the match in the third set super-tiebreak.</p>, <p>"On my serve I was confident. When I knew it was my serve, I knew we had this point. I was feeling it."</p>, <p>At the same time, number one seed Caroline Wozniacki made short work of German Laura Siegemund on centre court 6-3, 6-2.</p>, <p>That's now two comfortable wins for last year's finalists, with defending champ Julia Goerges cruising past 6-0, 6-4 yesterday.</p>, <p>While Paige Hourigan won't be troubling either of them in the singles, this will be a nice treat for what will be a big crowd later in the week her doubles semi final.</p>, <p>It was a scorcher today out on centre court, with the temperature around 38C at one point.</p>, <p>But that didn't deter another big turnout, which followed on from a sell out last night for the highly anticipated [https://www.radionz.co.nz/news/national/379316/pulsating-encounter-the-perfect-consolation</p>, <p>Venus Williams v Viktoria Azarenka] match, won by the American 6-3, 3-6, 6-3.</p>, <p class="copyright"><small>Copyright \xa9 <span itemprop="copyrightYear">2019</span>, <span itemprop="copyrightHolder">Radio New Zealand</span></small></p>, <p><i>Analysis</i> - If you're upset about Viktoria Azarenka having only one match at the latest edition of the ASB Classic, you can kind of blame <b>Jamie Wall</b>.</p>, <p>for ad-free news and current affairs</p>, <p>We have <a href="live-sport">regular online commentary</a> of local and international sport.</p>, <p><a class="btn btn-social btn-rss" href="/rss/sport.xml"><i class="icon-rss"></i>Sport RSS</a></p>, <p><a class="btn btn-social btn-twitter" href="https://twitter.com/rnz_news"><i class="icon-twitter"></i>Follow RNZ News</a></p>]
[<p>A report from the Italian press suggests that Max Allegri could leave Juventus in the summer with Zinedine Zidane coming in as his replacement.</p>, <p>The Livorno tactician has been at the club since 2014 having guided the Bianconeri to successive Serie A and Coppa Italia titles while losing two Champions League finals.</p>, <p>Top Planet journalist Luca Momblano now reports that Allegri is set to leave the club in summer, regardless of Juve\u2019s progression in Europe this season with a suggestion that a replacement has already been arranged.</p>, <p>Zinedine Zidane is reportedly lined up to take over from Allegri in the summer, having verbally agreed a deal with Juve President Andrea Agnelli.</p>, <p>The Frenchman left Real Madrid last summer having guided them to three consecutive Champions League titles.</p>, <p>Site Administrator and Owner. [<p>Even one of the nation's leading scorers knows it takes a team effort to knock off the No. 2 team in the nation.</p>, <p>The No. 18 Dakota Wesleyan University men's basketball team edged No. 2 Morningside College 86-82 in a Great Plains Athletic Conference men's basketball game on Wednesday at the Corn Palace.</p>, <p>DWU guard Ty Hoglund, who is the fifth leading scorer in the nation, pumped in 30 points and hit clutch shots late to bury the Mustangs. But Hoglund had plenty of help in handing Morningside College (14-1, 8-1) its first loss of the season.</p>, <p>"Not one guy can just beat that team," Hoglund said. "We had to have six-seven guys step up and that's what we did tonight."</p>, <p>The Tigers (13-4, 7-3 GPAC) used a second-half surge to put away the Mustangs, who entered the contest as the one of two undefeated teams in NAIA Division II.</p>, <p>"I thought it was a big-boy basketball game and I thought we had big performances all over the court," DWU coach Matt Wilber said. "That's a team basketball win and we were competing down the stretch."</p>, <p>DWU broke away from a 44-43 halftime advantage and built a 78-68 lead on a Hoglund 3-point play. The Mustangs took advantage of some missed shots by the Tigers and chopped the deficit to 80-76 with 1:30 left. Hoglund gave DWU some breathing room with a 3-pointer to make it 83-76 with 51 ticks left and it got the 2,531 fans at the Corn Palace rocking again.</p>, <p>"It's what I dreamt of as a kid, hitting a shot and the crowd goes crazy," Hoglund said. "Playing at the Corn Palace, there's nothing better. We have the best fans in the country. There's no doubt about that."</p>, <p>The Tigers converted at the free-throw line in the closing seconds to cap the victory.</p>, <p>Brody Egger scored 20 points for the Mustangs, while big man Tyler Borchers added 15 points and nine rebounds.</p>, <p>Nick Harden added 13 points and Aaron Ahmadu scored 12 points for the Tigers. Both teams battled foul trouble and the Tigers had a host of reserves make an impact.</p>, <p>"We had guys coming off the bench that were just constantly coming and contributing," DWU reserve post Tristan Teichmeier said. "This is the best overall game we played yet. It's just a great team win."</p>, <p>Teichmeier played 21 minutes as starter Sam McCloud was saddled with foul trouble and played 19 minutes, finishing with nine points. Teichmeier responded with 11 points (seven in the second half) and seven rebounds.</p>, <p>"I just was so encouraged and so happy for him because he's been dying to be productive for us and he's starting to be that way for us and good for him," Wilber said.</p>, <p>The 6-foot-6 Teichmeier drew the assignment of guarding the 6-foot-7 Borchers, who briefly left the game with a cut above his eye and returned with a bandage wrapped around his head.</p>, <p>"I have waited a long time to be able to play the game and I accepted it," Teichmeier said. "Wilber told me he's a big dude and he's big. I am not going to lie, but I was ready for it."</p>, <p>Mason Larson finished with four big rebounds and two steals. He hit just one of his four 3-point attempts, but it snapped a mini-Morningside run to stretch the lead back to 66-62 with 8:52 left.</p>, <p>"I know he missed a few shots, but he banged a big one and he's competing out there," Wilber said.</p>, <p>The action was back and forth in the opening minutes, with 10 lead changes in the first 6 1/2 minutes. The Mustangs pulled away and built an eight-point lead (24-16) with 10:48 left.</p>, <p>The Tigers weathered foul trouble and closed the first half with Teichmeier, Larson, Ahmadu, Cooper Williams and Collin Kramer. Ahmadu nailed a buzzer beater in the lane to make it 44-43 at halftime.</p>, <p>The teams traded shots in the early part of the second half before DWU pulled ahead.</p>, <p>"Everything about this was a team basketball win and that's who we are here," Wilber said. "We talk and preached about it. (It's) our culture and winning together and that's what these guys did."</p>, <p>The Tigers play at Dordt College on Wednesday, Jan. 9.</p>, <p></p>, <p><strong>No. 18 Dakota Wesleyan 86, No. 2 Morningside 82</strong></p>, <p><strong>Dakota Wesleyan (13-4, 7-3):</strong> Ty Hoglund 10-17 5-6 30, Nick Harden 5-10 3-6 13, Aaron Ahmadu 5-9 1-2 12, Tristan Teichmeier 4-7 3-7 11, Samuel McCloud 3-6 0-0 9, Mason Larson 1-4 0-0 3, Koln Oppold 0-4 0-0 0, Cooper Williams 0-1 0-0 0. Team totals: 31-65 12-21 86.</p>, <p><strong>Morningside (14-1, 8-1):</strong> Brody Egger 7-13 3-3 20, Tyler Borchers 7-13 1-3 15, Zach Imig 2-7 8-8 12, Alex Borchers 5-8 0-0 11, Matt Hahn 4-13 0-1 10, Pierce Almond 3-4 0-0 9, Trey Brown 2-3 0-0 4, Jeff Widhelm 0-1 1-2 1, Ben Hoskins 0-1 0-0 0, Andrew Semadeni 0-1 0-0 0, Trystan Cummins 0-1 0-0 0. Team totals: 30-65 13-17 82.</p>, <p>Halftime: DWU 44, M 43. 3-point field goals: DWU 12-34 (Hoglund 5-11, McCloud 3-6, Kramer 2-6, Ahmadu 1-3, Larson 1-4, Harden 0-2, Oppold 0-2); M 9-26 (Almond 3-4, Egger 3-9, Hahn 2-6, A. [<p class="label">\n\t\t\tTrending:\t\t</p>, <p>For the second time in less than a year, former San Francisco 49ers linebacker Reuben Foster has seen domestic violence charges against him dropped, TMZ Sports reported Thursday.</p>, <p>Foster\u2019s attorney Eddie Suarez said he believed the charges, related to a Nov. 24 incident at the 49ers team hotel in Tampa, were dropped due to \u201cissues with the witness\u2019 credibility,\u201d according to TMZ. Foster was scheduled for arraignment Thursday in Hillsborough County in Florida, but the hearing was canceled after prosecutors reportedly dropped the case.</p>, <p>Neither the\xa0Hillsborough County State Attorney\u2019s Office nor Suarez could be reached for comment by this news organization Thursday.</p>, <p>Shortly after Foster and estranged girlfriend Elissa Ennis got into the Nov. 24 altercation at the 49ers team hotel, Foster was <a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/11/25/49ers-release-reuben-foster-after-latest-domestic-violence-arrest/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">arrested and released by the 49ers</a>.\xa0Ennis soon after appeared on \u201cGood Morning America,\u201d where\xa0 she detailed the hotel encounter and\xa0<a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/12/06/reuben-fosters-accuser-breaks-silence-on-ex-49ers-alleged-domestic-violence/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">retracted her recantation in the Los Gatos case</a>.</p>, <p>It was the second time in the past 12 months that Foster was arrested on suspicion of domestic violence, with the\xa0<a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/02/12/reuben-foster-arrest-girlfriend-alleges-49ers-player-dragged-her-during-argument-sources-say/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">first occurring at their Los Gatos</a>\xa0home in February. Two felony domestic-violence related charges in that case were <a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/05/23/judge-to-decide-today-whether-reuben-foster-goes-to-trial/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">dismissed by a judge in May</a> when Ennis recanted the story she had told police. A third charge, for assault-rifle possession, was downgraded to a misdemeanor; Foster <a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/06/06/49ers-reuben-foster-pleads-no-contest-to-assault-rifle-charge/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pleaded no contest and was sentenced to probation</a>.</p>, <p>Santa Clara County District Attorney Jeff Rosen said after the Tampa arrest that his office was waiting for prosecutors there to complete their case before pursuing any legal options, including <a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/12/06/reuben-fosters-accuser-breaks-silence-on-ex-49ers-alleged-domestic-violence/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">whether to pursue a probation violation</a> for Foster. He also stated that Ennis will face no perjury charges stemming from the TV interview where she confessed to lying on the stand to protect Foster.</p>, <p>Thursday, Rosen\u2019s office issued a statement reiterating that prosecutors are still evaluating the Foster situation.</p>, <p>\u201cMr. Foster remains on probation for his misdemeanor conviction in Santa Clara County,\u201d the statement reads. \u201cWould a court in Santa Clara County, California consider an allegation that did not result in a criminal charge in another state to be a basis for a violation of his court probation condition to obey all laws? We are looking into it.\u201d</p>, <p>The 49ers declined to comment after the news that the Florida charges were dropped against Foster. But after the organization cut him from the team, General Manager John Lynch said,\xa0\u201cI was very direct with him, that if he didn\u2019t prove to us that we could trust how he made decisions it didn\u2019t matter whether he was right or wrong \u2026 That\u2019s the consequences of life. If you put yourself in those situations, that\u2019s not OK with us.\u201d</p>, <p>Also after the Florida arrest, news surfaced that Foster and Ennis were the subject of a <a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/12/11/santa-clara-city-re-releases-video-of-reuben-foster-domestic-call-with-unredacted-audio/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">domestic-violence call at an apartment in Santa Clara in October,</a> but one was arrested after police said they found no evidence of a crime. But they told police that they lived together, indicating that they reconciled after the Los Gatos case was dismissed.</p>, <p>On \u201cGood Morning America,\u201d Ennis described how she had reconnected with Foster and how his latest arrest unfolded.</p>, <p>\u201cHe called me to come see him in Florida,\u201d she said. \u201cAnd I came and he took one of my phones and he slapped me and pushed me. I told him I was going to tell his new girlfriend that he paid for my flight out there, so that\u2019s what triggered it.</p>, <p>\u201cHe called me out there so we could work on our relationship. And so I was, \u2018I can\u2019t believe he\u2019d be back to doing this because we both were seeing therapists.\u2019 \u201d</p>, <p>Within days of being released by the 49ers, Foster was <a href="https://www.mercurynews.com/2018/11/27/which-nfl-team-claimed-reuben-foster-off-waivers-from-49ers/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">picked up by Washington</a>. The team was criticized, and said Foster would not suit up for them until the legal process was resolved.</p>, <p class="prompt">Get Morning Report and other email newsletters</p>]

[<p class="posted"><strong>Posted:</strong> Jan 03, 2019 04:44 PM EST</p>, <p class="updated"><strong>Updated:</strong> Jan 03, 2019 06:59 PM EST</p>, <p class="crop-ellipsis toggle"> Muhammad Ali's estate near Berrien Springs. (June 19, 2018) <span class="toggler">\xa0[<a class="trigger maximize" href="#">\xa0+\xa0</a><a class="trigger minimize" href="#">\xa0-\xa0</a>]</span></p>, <p>ORONOKO TOWNSHIP, Mich. (WOOD) \u2014 An estate near Berrien Springs that used to belong to legendary boxer Muhammad Ali has been sold.</p>, <p>The home sold Dec. 21 for $2.5 million, <a href="https://timmitchell.cressyeverett.com/p/8105-Kephart-Lane-Berrien-Springs-MI-49103/dmgsid_31671237" target="_blank"><strong>according to the real estate agency</strong></a> handling the sale.</p>, <p>Located on Kephart Lane just outside the village, the 100-year-old farmhouse sits on 81 acres. It boasts three bedrooms, two full baths, a gym where Ali trained during the peak of his career, and a pool. Ali and his wife Lonnie Ali spent their retirement there.</p>, <p>The house also previously belonged to Al Capone lieutenant Louis Campagna.</p>, <p>The original asking price was nearly $2.9 million when the home <a href="https://www.woodtv.com/news/southwest-michigan/inside-muhammad-ali-s-berrien-springs-estate/1249742904"><strong>went on the market</strong></a> in June 2018.</p>, <p> <aside class="mod-inline media none"> <figure> <div class="image-wrapper"> <a class="meta category overlay" data-reveal-id="modal-gallery-photos-1249763395" href="#">22 Photos</a> <a class="add-magnify-icon" data-reveal-id="modal-gallery-photos-1249763395" href="#"> <img alt="photo" src="https://media.woodtv.com/nxs-woodtv-media-us-east-1/photo/2018/06/19/5_1529449683878_46028824_ver1.0_640_360.jpg"/> <small class="copyright">Copyright 2019 Nexstar Broadcasting, Inc.
