[<p>Cloudy. Low 38F. Winds W at 10 to 15 mph..</p>, <p>Cloudy. Low 38F. Winds W at 10 to 15 mph.</p>, <p class="text-center"><small><i class="fas tnt-info-circle"></i> Updated: January 3, 2019 @ 5:22 pm</small></p>, <p>Colorado head coach Tad Boyle and Arizona head coach Sean Miller both use the same gesture to organize their teams in the second half of their Pac-12 game at McKale Center, Thursday, January 25, 2018, Tucson, Ariz.</p>, <p>Colorado head coach Tad Boyle and Arizona head coach Sean Miller both use the same gesture to organize their teams in the second half of their Pac-12 game at McKale Center, Thursday, January 25, 2018, Tucson, Ariz.</p>, <p>Maybe it was playing at sea level over in Hawaii that did the Buffs in.</p>, <p>Since joining the Pac-12 in 2011-12, Colorado has struggled to play nearly as well at lower elevation road environments as it does at the mile-high Coors Events Center in Boulder. They are 7-29 in Pac-12 games away from home since 2013-14, with no more than two conference road wins per season since then.</p>, <p>While the Buffs have managed to win two road games already this season, those were also both at high altitude: At Air Force and at New Mexico.</p>, <p>Thursday\u2019s test at McKale will be held at roughly halfway between sea level and Boulder\u2019s elevation of 5,328 feet.</p>, <p>However, sophomore wing D\u2019Shawn Schwartz appeared confident that the Buffs can win anywhere on the road this season.</p>, <p>\u201cThere\u2019s not a team in (the league) that I don\u2019t think we can beat,\u201d Schwartz told <a href="http://Buffzone.com">Buffzone.com</a>. \u201cI think we can get some road wins, as opposed to last year. We\u2019ve grown a little bit, and I think we have a chance to get some road wins starting on the third.\u201d</p>, <p>\u201cWe just did it a couple weeks before Christmas when we went to New Mexico. The buildings are similar. The fan base is really into it and educated. [<p>Liberty\u2019s coaching staff sent out the wrong wrestler at 145 pounds.</p>, <p>All freshman Christian Reid did in his first varsity match was cover for the coaches by delivering an improbable pin.</p>, <p>\u201cIt was a rookie coaching mistake,\u201d Hurricanes coach Jody Karam said. \u201cWe made a serious mistake. The wrong kid went out. It was too late to bring him back. As a head coach, I accept full responsibility for it.</p>, <p>\u201cBut, nothing went as scripted tonight.\u201d</p>, <p>Making Reid\u2019s win more impressive \u2014 and important \u2014 was that he was losing 7-1 midway through the third period before getting the reverse and headlock to secure the six points in 5 minutes, 22 seconds.</p>, <p>There were other heroes for Liberty during Wednesday\u2019s 32-28 EPC win over host Northampton.</p>, <p>With the home side of Pete Schneider Gym going crazy after Jayden Bortz beat Damen Moyer 7-6 at 195 pounds to give the Konkrete Kids a 28-17 lead, Jake Ahmad needed 40 seconds to give the Hurricanes the momentum back.</p>, <p>Jaden Freeman made sure Liberty didn\u2019t let it go. The senior 285-pounder secured a takedown in the last two seconds to win 4-3.</p>, <p>Connor Werner scored a takedown halfway through the first period, then took advantage of a mistake with 40 seconds left at 106 and turned it into a five-point move and a 7-0 win.</p>, <p>That left hammer Tal-Reese Flemming, a returning state bronze medalist, to clinch the match.</p>, <p>The senior 113-pounder got an early takedown, but then was ridden out for the second period and most of the third before getting a reversal with four seconds left to give Liberty the win.</p>, <p>\u201cThis is what makes Lehigh Valley wrestling fun,\u201d Karam said. \u201cYou can\u2019t pay for what we got tonight.</p>, <p>\u201cNothing buys you this feeling. Christian Reid, man, losing the match, and typical Liberty guts. And, [Connor] Werner with the big win and Jake Ahmad, those three guys really turned it around for us.\u201d</p>, <p>For the Konkrete Kids, it was an opportunity missed.</p>, <p>\u201cFor a little while there, we felt like we had them right where we needed them,\u201d Northampton coach Seth Lisa said.</p>, <p>\u201cWe knew some type of shift was going to happen, able to get matchup we wanted at 145, up 7-1 going for major, get pinned in a headlock. Not beating a team as good as Liberty when your guys are losing bouts like that.</p>, <p>\u201cAt heavyweight, you\u2019re beating a really good kid, then get taken down with no time on clock. That cost us the match.</p>, <p>\u201cAt 106, we tried a silly move you thought was going to help you score. You have to understand the sport to realize the basics win the match.\u201d</p>, <p>\u201cWe got a lot to learn from this. \u2026 We\u2019re most certainly going to wrestle them again. This was a trial run. \u201d</p>, <p>After losing the opener, Northampton won five of six bouts, all with bonus points, to build a 25-10 lead.</p>, <p>Bortz then pulled off the upset of Moyer, who had pinned him twice in previous matches. It didn\u2019t come easy, though. Bortz got a reversal with 1:17 left in the match, then had to survive two caution calls in the final four seconds.</p>, <p>Liberty hosts Bethlehem Catholic on Friday. Northampton takes part in Parkland\u2019s Winter Duals on Saturday.</p>, <p><strong>Liberty 32, Northampton 28</strong></p>, <p><strong>106</strong>: Connor Werner (L) dec. [<p id="weatherChange"></p>, <p class="byline ap-byline">Rhiannon Potkey, Associated Press</p>, <p class="open">Caption</p>, <p class="close">Close</p>, <p>KNOXVILLE, Tenn. (AP) \u2014 Tennessee head coach Holly Warlick wants to see her young team mature into productive college players.</p>, <p>But as she watched Belmont continually drive to the basket and beat the Lady Vols on backdoor cuts, Warlick wanted to put her players in a fundamental time machine.</p>, <p>"Go back to elementary school - the ball, you and the basket," Warlick said. "Stay between the ball and the basket and forget about what happened on the other end. You have to have a short-term memory when you make a mistake."</p>, <p>Evina Westbrook scored 20 points and sparked a late flurry as the No. 10 Lady Vols held off Belmont 84-76 on Sunday in their final tune-up before Southeastern Conference play begins.</p>, <p>Rennia Davis scored 19 points and Meme Jackson and Zaay Green each had 10 for Tennessee, which received a wake-up call on defense in the second half against the gritty Bruins.</p>, <p>Belmont (7-4), a perennial mid-major contender, gave the Lady Vols (11-1) all they could handle, rallying from an 18-point first-half deficit to take a brief lead in the fourth quarter.</p>, <p>But Tennessee managed to hit enough shots down the stretch to avoid the upset in the first meeting between the in-state programs since 1979.</p>, <p>Ellie Harmeyer finished with 20 points and 10 rebounds for Belmont, which outscored Tennessee 50-34 in the paint. Darby Maggard finished with 14 points, Maura Muensterman had 12 and Maddie Wright scored 10.</p>, <p>Belmont entered the game averaging 10 made 3-pointers per game to rank No. 11 in the nation. The Lady Vols focused on running them off the 3-point line, and it worked. The Bruins finished only 4 of 20 from behind the arc while Tennessee was hot from outside early.</p>, <p>The Lady Vols had never hit seven or more 3-pointers in five straight games, but easily reached that milestone by halftime.</p>, <p>Tennessee finished 9 of 13 from deep through two quarters to enter the break with a seemingly comfortable 51-35 advantage.</p>, <p>But the Lady Vols would go cold from deep, failing to hit another 3-pointer for the remainder of the game.</p>, <p>Belmont went inside to stage its comeback, pushing around the Lady Vols near the rim and out-hustling them for loose balls. The Bruins outscored Tennessee 23-8 in the third quarter to trim the deficit to 59-58.</p>, <p>Maggard gave the Bruins their first lead since early in the first quarter with a layup for a 64-63 edge with 6:12 remaining.</p>, <p>"They chose to play small for a lot of stretches there in the second half, so we were able to get some stuff to Ellie and Maddie inside on post ups," Belmont head coach Bart Brooks said. "But most of our inside stuff was back cuts and dribble drives and floor spacing. We expected that because of how they pressured the ball."</p>, <p>The teams traded baskets in the fourth quarter before Westbrook helped spark a late run for the Lady Vols to remain in front for good.</p>, <p>BIG PICTURE</p>, <p>Belmont: The Ohio Valley Conference favorites played a challenging pre-conference schedule to prepare for their title defense. The Bruins faced three Power 5 conference teams, including two ranked in the AP Top 25 - No. 9 North Carolina State and No. 10 Tennessee. Belmont has yet to beat a ranked opponent since transitioning to Division I in 1997, falling to 0-20 all-time. But the second-half performance against the Lady Vols gives the Bruins some confidence.</p>, <p>"We came in here ready to win," Maggard said. "Honestly, it is really encouraging. We are going to take this game and learn more from it and keep moving forward. I think playing teams like this is only going to help us in our conference and down the road when we are hopefully in big-time games in March."</p>, <p>Tennessee: With six freshmen and sophomores playing more than 13 minutes per game, the youthful Lady Vols have to be happy with their record entering conference play. But they have to be concerned with how easily Belmont pushed them around inside in the second half as they prepare for the rigors of the SEC. Tennessee's only loss came to No. 6 Stanford, and they beat No. 13 Texas on the road.</p>, <p>ALL THAT JAZZ</p>, <p>Tennessee freshman guard Jazmine Massengill scored seven points and grabbed five rebounds for the Lady Vols, one game after recording a career-high 10 points against Murray State. The Lady Vols have been encouraging Massengill to look for her shot more when she's open to help keep defenses honest.</p>, <p>"It is amazing. I had a talk with her before I came in here and said, 'Great game. You just have to be consistent and keep shooting the ball,'" Westbrook said.</p>, <p>HISTORY LESSON</p>, <p>Warlick was a point guard leading Pat Summitt's team the last time these programs met in 1979. Warlick scored 15 points in a 94-53 win over the Bruins in the first round of the Tennessee College Women's Sports Federation Tournament at Stokely Athletics Center in Knoxville.</p>, <p>UP NEXT</p>, <p>Belmont opens Ohio Valley Conference play against Jacksonville State on Thursday at home.</p>, <p>Tennessee opens Southeastern Conference play against Auburn on Thursday on the road.</p>]

[<p>\n<span class="ng_byline_name">By JEROME PUGMIRE </span><span class="ng_byline_credit">AP Sports Writer</span>\n</p>, <p id="publish_date">January 03, 2019 12:02 AM<span></span></p>, <p id="update_date"></p>, <p>Against the backdrop of celebrations marking Michael Schumacher's 50th birthday on Thursday, the medical condition of Formula One's most successful driver remains just as fiercely guarded by his close family.</p>, <p>More than five years after a near-fatal brain injury in a skiing accident, the seven-time F1 champion continues to be cared for in total secrecy at home in the quiet Swiss town of Gland on the shores of Lake Geneva. He has been there since being transferred from a hospital in September 2014.</p>, <p>"You can be sure that he is in the very best of hands and that we are doing everything humanly possible to help him," Schumacher's family said in a rare statement Wednesday. "Please understand if we are following Michael's wishes and keeping such a sensitive subject as health, as it has always been, in privacy."</p>, <p>It was while skiing with his teenage son Mick in the French Alps at Meribel that Schumacher fell on Dec. 29, 2013. He hit the right side of his head on a rock, splitting open his helmet. Doctors at Grenoble hospital removed blood clots, but others were left untouched because too deeply embedded in his brain.</p>, <p>Last chance to take advantage of our best offer of the year!  Act now!</p>, <p>#ReadLocal</p>, <p>With unsourced stories abounding, updates on his condition went from scarce to non-existent as his family closed ranks around him . But the family understands the level of devotion toward Schumacher from his legions of fans.</p>, <p>Coinciding with his birthday, the family is releasing the Official Michael Schumacher App offering a virtual museum tour of his greatest achievements.</p>, <p>"The app is another milestone in our effort to do justice to him and you, his fans, by celebrating his accomplishments," the statement said.</p>, <p>Many of those accomplishments were with Ferrari, where the German driving ace won five titles. The Italian manufacturer is honoring his 50th with a special museum exhibition of his achievements at its Maranello headquarters in northern Italy.</p>, <p>His stature is Ferrari folklore is immense, while his impact on F1 is unparalleled with perhaps the exception of the late Brazilian great Ayrton Senna.</p>, <p>Schumacher's winners' aura was perhaps unfairly viewed from the outside as cold and distant, when in essence he was incredibly appreciative of those he worked closely with. In 2000, he delivered Ferrari from years of frustration with a first world title since Jody Scheckter in 1979.</p>, <p>At the time, Schumacher spoke about the emotions he felt as the team celebrated wildly around him.</p>, <p>"Those faces. Bright eyes everywhere and everyone cheering," Schumacher said in recognition. "I would have loved to hug and kiss each and every one of them."</p>, <p>Schumacher won the next four F1 titles \u2014 even securing the 2002 title an astonishing six races before the end \u2014 on his way to a record 91 GP wins. His speed, consistency and work ethic were all unmatched.</p>, <p>"He was winning races sometimes he shouldn't have won," said F1's managing director Ross Brawn, who worked with Schumacher on all seven F1 titles. "He just had a majesty about him in that period."</p>, <p>During Schumacher's glory years, F1 even rivalled soccer as the No. 1 sport in Italy \u2014 quite an achievement. Memorabilia from those halcyon days, including cars and race-worn helmets, has been on display in the German city of Cologne at The Michael Schumacher Private Collection since June of last year.</p>, <p>"Michael can be proud of what he has achieved, and so are we," his family's statement said. "We want to remember and celebrate his victories, his records and his jubilation."</p>, <p>Schumacher has not been seen in public since his accident.</p>, <p>Brawn and Jean Todt \u2014 the head of motorsport's governing body FIA \u2014 are very close friends and have visited him at his Swiss home. Brawn reiterated the need for Schumacher to be shielded from the media spotlight.</p>, <p>"I am constantly in touch with (Schumacher's wife) Corinna and I totally agree with their decision," Brawn said. "Michael has always been a very private person."</p>, <p>The exhibitions in Cologne and Maranello are initiatives of the Keep Fighting Foundation, launched by Schumacher's family and of which Brawn and Todt are trustees.</p>, <p>RISING STAR</p>, <p>It was then-Ferrari general manager Todt who persuaded Schumacher to join him there after world titles with Benetton in 1994 and 1995, where he had developed a dazzlingly successful rapport with Brawn.</p>, <p>Todt rarely speaks publicly about Schumacher, out of respect, but revealed he watched the Brazilian GP with Schumacher at his Switzerland home in November.</p>, <p>Brawn spotted the young Schumacher's brazen talent during the World Sportscar Championship.</p>, <p>"He was doing lap times on less fuel than the others, and beating them by a mile," Brawn said, underling how even then Schumacher was "clearly incredibly quick."</p>, <p>They started working together at Benetton in 1991. A year later, Schumacher won his first F1 race at the Belgian GP and his astonishing career took off.</p>, <p>"In '94 when he won the first championship he was incredible," Brawn said.</p>, <p>Given his age and lack of experience at the time, Schumacher's breakthrough Benetton days were arguably equal to his stellar time with Ferrari.</p>, <p>"It's difficult to define a peak," Brawn told F1's official podcast.</p>, <p>HAMILTON CLOSING IN</p>, <p>                Five-time F1 champion Lewis Hamilton has Schumacher's records within his sights, and age relatively on his side.</p>, <p>Given that the British driver is contracted with Mercedes for at least this season and next, he has a strong chance of equaling Schumacher's seven titles and number of race wins.</p>, <p>The 33-year-old Hamilton has won 73 races \u2014 18 behind but with a slightly higher win ratio than Schumacher had.</p>, <p>Hamilton, arguably F1's greatest ever talent in qualifying, has eclipsed Schumacher's record for pole positions: 83-68.</p>, <p>They are level for most podiums in a season with 17. But Schumacher leads him in terms of consecutive podiums finishes overall 19-16, as well as fastest laps with a staggering 77-41.</p>, <p>Schumacher also holds the F1 record for most wins at a single race: eight at the French GP.</p>, <p>RISING SON</p>, <p>Having raced against Schumacher in F1 and then replaced him at Mercedes, Hamilton could well end up driving against Schumacher's son.</p>, <p>All eyes will be on Mick Schumacher this year as he competes in F2 with the Prema Racing team.</p>, <p>The 19-year-old Schumacher won last year's F3 championship in style with eight wins and seven pole positions.</p>, <p>It was another racing title for the Schumacher family, and maybe not the last.</p>, <p>If Schumacher wins the F2 championship in 2019 then he, like other drivers such as Ferrari's Charles Leclerc, could well be fast-tracked into F1.</p>, <p>\n<span class="ng_byline_name">By MICHAEL TARM </span><span class="ng_byline_credit">Associated Press</span>\n</p>, <p id="publish_date">January 03, 2019 06:26 PM<span></span></p>, <p id="update_date"></p>, <p>One of the most powerful and longest-serving City Council members in Chicago history has appeared in federal court on a charge that he tried to shake down a major fast-food restaurant chain seeking city remodeling permits.</p>, <p>#ReadLocal</p>, <p>Last chance to take advantage of our best offer of the year!  Act now!</p>, <p>Real-time updates and all local stories you want right in the palm of your hand.</p>]
[<p data-page="1">To be affiliated with UCLA basketball is to dream.</p>, <p>To dream of becoming the program that properly collects and nurtures Southern California\u2019s reservoir of talent. To dream of returning to national prominence. To dream of recapturing the magic from the period when John Wooden was coach.</p>, <p>Reality is optional.</p>, <p>Now that Steve Alford has been fired, UCLA is dreaming again, more specifically about his permanent replacement and how that next coach will do what he couldn\u2019t.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.latimes.com/sports/ucla/la-sp-lakers-lonzo-ball-ucla-earl-watson-20190102-story.html" target="_blank">While some prominent alumni have started advocating for former Bruins point guard Earl Watson</a>, the school\u2019s fantasy appointment remains Billy Donovan, the architect of the Florida program that won consecutive national championships in 2006 and 2007.</p>, <p>Two days after Alford\u2019s dismissal, Donovan happened to be in Los Angeles, about 10 miles from Pauley Pavilion. He wasn\u2019t here to stump for the UCLA post, but to coach his Oklahoma City Thunder against the Lakers at Staples Center.</p>, <p>Donovan said pretty much what would be expected from a coach under contract.</p>, <p>\u201cWe have a great group of guys and I\u2019ve enjoyed, really, working with these guys each and every day,\u201d he said. \u201cMy focus is totally on the Thunder right now.\u201d</p>, <p>Donovan\u2019s All-Star guard, Russell Westbrook, wouldn\u2019t get involved in the discussion. Asked for his thoughts on what his alma mater should do, Westbrook replied, \u201cIt ain\u2019t up to me, champ.\u201d</p>, <p>Westbrook is a UCLA donor, however. The Bruins\u2019 practice court is named after him.</p>, <p>\u201cI ain\u2019t that big of a damn donor,\u201d he wisecracked.</p>, <p>To be clear, the chances of UCLA landing Donovan are remote. The Thunder recently exercised his option for the 2019-20 season, meaning he almost certainly won\u2019t be available when UCLA intensifies its search in the coming months.</p>, <p>But for the argument\u2019s sake, let\u2019s say UCLA can figure out a way to free Donovan from his deal. Would he really want a move to Westwood?</p>, <p>The Thunder entered Wednesday in third place in the Western Conference. The team has a couple of superstars in Westbrook and Paul George.</p>, <p>Alford earned $2.6 million annually. Even if UCLA goes all Chip Kelly and doubles that figure for its next coach, it will be less than Donovan\u2019s average annual salary of $6 million with the Thunder.</p>, <p>What the 53-year-old Donovan did say was recruiting obligations wouldn\u2019t be what deters him from returning to college basketball.</p>, <p>\u201cI think a lot of times, to be honest with you, sometimes that gets overblown,\u201d Donovan said. \u201cI think there\u2019s this feeling that guys that have made the jump from college to the NBA left because of recruiting. I never felt that way. I always enjoyed recruiting. I liked recruiting.\u201d</p>, <p>Donovan spent more than two decades on the recruiting trail before he was appointed coach of the Thunder in 2015.</p>, <p>He started coaching as an assistant to then-Kentucky coach Rick Pitino, under whom he was a standout point guard at Providence. His first head coaching job consisted of a two-year stint at Marshall, after which he took over Florida at the age of 30.</p>, <p>Donovan constructed the program at Florida from the ground up. The school experienced limited basketball glory before his arrival. Over his 19 seasons with the Gators, he enjoyed the kind of sustained success UCLA is craving \u2014 four Final Fours, seven Elite Eights, 14 NCAA tournament appearances and 16 consecutive 20-win seasons.</p>, <p>The train wreck at UCLA can in part be traced back to him. Florida\u2019s opponent in the 2006 national championship game was UCLA. Florida\u2019s opponent in the 2007 national semifinal was also UCLA. The Bruins win those games and, who knows, maybe the second half of Ben Howland\u2019s reign would have played out differently.</p>, <p>So there was no truth to reports Donovan moved to the Thunder in part because he was exhausted of recruiting?</p>, <p>\u201cI think there\u2019s a lot of speculation \u2026\u201d he started.</p>, <p>He caught himself and asked a question in return: \u201cDid I say that?\u201d</p>, <p>No.</p>, <p>\u201cOK,\u201d he said with a smile.</p>, <p>Donovan continued, \u201cPeople say that all the time about different things and I don\u2019t think I\u2019ve ever said that. I\u2019ve always enjoyed the time that I had to recruit and meet different people and those kinds of things. Is it a lot of work? Yeah. Is it a lot of effort? Yes.\u201d</p>, <p>Sounds promising for UCLA? Well, here comes the \u201cbut\u201d \u2026</p>, <p>\u201cWhen the season ended in March, you couldn\u2019t really do anything basketball-wise,\u201d Donovan said. \u201cThere was a lot of time. I feel like in the NBA, it\u2019s 12 months a year you\u2019re thinking about your team and you\u2019re thinking about basketball. I don\u2019t think that the notion that guys that leave college to go to the NBA is all because they don\u2019t want to recruit. I don\u2019t think it has anything to do with that. I think you\u2019ll probably find most basketball coaches in college would love to be able to do basketball more than they\u2019ve been able to do.\u201d</p>, <p>He later reiterated that what he likes about the NBA is that \u201cyou\u2019re just dealing with basketball all day long.\u201d</p>, <p>So Donovan didn\u2019t exactly open the door for a move to Westwood. Then again, he didn\u2019t completely close it, either.</p>, <p>That will have to suffice for UCLA, where reality rarely lives up to the dream.</p>]

[<p>Updated at 5:03 p.m. ET</p>, <p>Updated at 5:03 p.m. ET</p>, <p>After former USC assistant coach Tony Bland stood in federal court and admitted he had committed a felony \u2014 conspiracy to commit bribery \u2014 his attorney stood before the media and called the most clich\xe9d play in the college basketball playbook.</p>, <p>Not the pick-and-roll or the give-and-go or shouting, \u201cThe butler did it!\u201d</p>, <p>He blamed the NCAA.</p>, <p><strong>FACES OF 2019<br/><a href="https://www.sportingnews.com/us/sport/features/sporting-news-players-athletes-to-watch-in-2019">SN selects young stars who will shape tomorrow's headlines</a></strong></p>, <p>\u201cThis is a case that is a product of a very broken, antiquated system,\u201d attorney Jeffrey Lichtman told reporters afterward, according to the <a href="https://www.latimes.com/sports/sportsnow/la-sp-tony-bland-guilty-20190102-story.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Los Angeles Times</a>. \u201cHe was looking to help the players, but the problem is the way he went about it was wrong.</p>, <p>\u201cIf the NCAA is unwilling to police itself, I have respect for the Southern District of New York prosecutors for being willing to do it. This is a broken system.\u201d</p>, <p>It was a curious call \u2014 kind of like a fake-punt run by a fullback on fourth-and-5 \u2014 given that the count to which Bland pleaded guilty did not involve the sort of pay-for-players allegations that led to guilty verdicts in the fall against two former Adidas executives and a former agency representative.\xa0</p>, <p>Really, now, what role would the NCAA possibly have in regard\xa0to the count that led to Bland\u2019s plea? He acknowledged that, while he was employed as an assistant coach at Southern California, he accepted a $4,100 bribe as incentive to direct young athletes to employ a management firm headed by Munish Sood and Christian Dawkins.</p>, <p>\u201cWhatever the rules, taking money behind someone\u2019s back to steer him to an agent or financial adviser is wrong and illegal,\u201d an agency financial manager who wished to remain anonymous\xa0told Sporting News. \u201cAnd if the NCAA changed its amateurism rules, it would still be illegal to deal surreptitiously.\u201d</p>, <p>This charge was similar to the case against former Auburn assistant coach Chuck Person, which is set to go to trial next month. These circumstances have gained less attention than what was described during the trial of <a href="http://www.sportingnews.com/us/ncaa-basketball/news/college-basketball-corruption-trial-adidas-executives-ncaa-guilty-verdict-james-gatto-christian-dawkins-merl-code/1rx5f89spid3111nwauvijvlkf">Jim Gatto, Merl Code and Dawkins</a> last September,\xa0because the media always seem to focus more on alleged cheating creating a competitive advantage than the actions that can engender genuine victims. But what Bland has admitted and what Person will face at trial represents the most repulsive aspect of the government\u2019s case.</p>, <p>In a statement, U.S. attorney Geoffrey Berman said Bland \u201cabused his position as a mentor and coach to student-athletes and aspiring professionals. He treated his players not as young men to counsel and guide, but as opportunities to enrich himself.\u201d</p>, <p><strong>SPORTING NEWS BEST OF 2018<br/><a href="https://www.sportingnews.com/us/sport/features/best-of-2018">Read our\xa0favorite stories from the year in sports</a></strong></p>, <p>Person has been charged with receiving more than $90,000, in part as incentive to direct athletes to Pittsburgh-based financial manager Marty Blazer. A simple Google search shows that Blazer in May 2016 <a href="https://triblive.com/business/headlines/10429527-74/blazer-financial-money" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">faced a civil suit by the Securities and Exchange Commission</a> for allegedly taking $2.35 million from athletes' accounts as part of a Ponzi scheme. He was eventually ordered to pay <a href="https://www.sec.gov/litigation/litreleases/2017/lr23900.htm" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">about $1.8 million</a>.</p>, <p>Bland originally had been accused of accepting a $13,000 bribe, but the <a href="https://www.latimes.com/sports/usc/la-sp-college-basketball-bland-20181116-story.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Los Angeles Times reported</a> that Dawkins\xa0made a deposit of $8,900 at a Las Vegas bank on\xa0the same day in August 2017 that the bribe was alleged to have occurred. The figure to which Bland admitted accepting apparently represents the difference between Dawkins' deposit and the original figure Bland was accused of receiving.</p>, <p>However, if Bland had used Google to look up Dawkins in advance of their meeting, he likely would have <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/lookit/2017/5/4/15549768/sports-agent-fired-42000-in-uber-charges-nba-players-credit-card" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">discovered a story</a> about Dawkins losing his position at ASM Sports after it was alleged he\u2019d used an athlete\u2019s account to ring up $42,000 in Uber fares. Whether Bland knew of this in advance of their meeting was not germane to the government\u2019s case, but the ease of access to this information demonstrates how indefensible Bland\u2019s actions were in accepting the bribe.</p>, <p>In court, of course, Bland was entitled to a defense, and he got one. He is expected to receive probation, and the outcome certainly could have been worse. Afterward, Lichtman called Bland \u201cthe most decent man\u201d he had represented.</p>, <p>That plea for your sympathy \u2014 as did his call for antipathy toward the NCAA \u2014 fell more than a few yards short.</p>]

[<p></p>, <p>HOUSTON\u2014<a href="http://bleacherreport.com/james-harden">James Harden</a> normally doesn't have a propensity to pontificate about himself or his exploits on the court. Whenever\xa0he's questioned about basketball, he's succinct, reserved, contemplative.\xa0He lets his game do the talking.</p>, <p><span>And for the month of December, it was record-breaking.</span></p>, <p><span>The <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/nba">NBA</a>'s reigning MVP scored 408 points, dished out 89 assists and pulled down 68 rebounds over his last 10 games.\xa0</span>It was the most points, assists and rebounds logged over a 10-game span by any player in <a href="https://twitter.com/NBA/status/1080214629366804480" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">NBA history</a>.\xa0But as impressive as those stats were, they weren't loud enough.</p>, <p><span>Perhaps annoyed by the viral memes attacking his step-back jumper and various trolling comments proliferating the internet, Harden erupted with an impassioned statement about securing back-to-back MVPs that sent a jolt through the league like a crack of thunder.</span></p>, <p><span>"Of course I should be in that conversation. I mean, I receive a lot of hate, but it won't stop me from going out there and killing every single night, being that dog that I am," <span>Harden said with a hint of bluster last week</span>. "You can name a few other people that should be in the conversation. But realistically? It's coming back."</span></p>, <p><span>That was quite the quote from a player whose sartorial whims speak louder than he does. But as the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/houston-rockets">Houston Rockets</a> (21-15) begin their new year with a nationally televised game against the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/golden-state-warriors">Golden State Warriors</a> in Oracle Arena on Thursday, he opted for the exclamation point.</span></p>, <p><span>"I need it. I need it for sure," Harden told Bleacher Report's\xa0<a href="https://bleacherreport.com/articles/2813620-rockets-james-harden-on-winning-a-2nd-mvp-need-it-for-sure-and-im-getting-it" target="_blank">Will Gottlieb</a>\xa0when asked if he's hungry for winning another MVP. "And I'm going to get it."</span></p>, <p>There it is. One of Harden's resolutions for 2019 is earning another\xa0Maurice Podoloff Trophy.</p>, <p>But does he deserve it?</p>, <p>The judging guidelines for MVP are subjective and esoteric, but if the judges focus solely on numbers, Harden has an airtight case.</p>, <p>"He's by far the MVP," head coach Mike D'Antoni said. "Nobody does what he does on a nightly basis."</p>, <p>The Western Conference Player of the Week recorded his fourth triple-double of the season Monday night with 43 points, 10 rebounds and 13 assists in the Rockets' 113-101 win over the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/memphis-grizzlies">Memphis Grizzlies</a> and his eighth straight game with at least 35 points and five assists, passing Oscar Robertson for the record.\xa0He also joined Michael Jordan and <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/kobe-bryant">Kobe Bryant</a> as the third player\xa0over the last 30 years to drop at least 400 points over 10 games.</p>, <p><span>With The Beard's dominant finish to 2018, Houston moved from 14th to fourth in the Western Conference.</span></p>, <p>"I don't know how you get any better than what he's playing," D'Antoni added. "Defensively, too. He comes up with steals, triple-doubles like it's nothing. So, yeah, he's playing at a different level."</p>, <p>Harden hit another gear during the Rockets' recent 10-1 run, averaging an eye-popping 39.7 points, 8.5 assists, 6.3 rebounds, 2.1 steals and 5.5 made three-pointers per game, but critics won't easily forget how the team started the season.</p>, <p>At the beginning of last month, only the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/phoenix-suns">Phoenix Suns</a> had a worse record in the West.\xa0Houston started at 11-14, and that grated at Harden, so he went to work.</p>, <p>"He comes in and does extra work," D'Antoni said. "He knew he had to take his body to one more level up. He had to get into a better rhythm. He's been playing a lot of one-on-one. He's been doing a lot of extra work in the weight room. He's been putting his time in. Obviously, it's paying dividends."</p>, <p>Harden is averaging a league-leading 33.3 points per contest, the highest scoring average since Bryant's 35.4 points per game in 2005-06.\xa0He's also stepped forward as a leader, making sure his teammates are as locked in as he is.</p>, <p>"He's making sure guys get extra work in after practice," Gerald Green said. "Making sure guys are focused on pregame. He does a lot of little things you probably don't see on camera."</p>, <p>Harden's array of three-pointers, Eurosteps in the lane, tomahawk dunks and crafty passes may come off as entertaining on camera, but there's something else that comes through just as clearly as the highlights: his high usage rate.</p>, <p>At <a href="https://stats.nba.com/players/advanced/?sort=USG_PCT&amp;dir=-1&amp;CF=MIN*GE*15&amp;Season=2018-19&amp;SeasonType=Regular%20Season" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">37.4</a>, he has the ball in his hands a lot, and that level of play can be exhausting and unsustainable.\xa0Will Harden get burned out from being a one-man show?</p>, <p>With <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/chris-paul">Chris Paul</a> sidelined long term with a hamstring injury and Eric Gordon out with a right knee contusion, it's not surprising that the bat signal went up in Space City and Harden had to answer the call with a December to remember.</p>, <p>But as the season unfolds, his numbers will eventually come back to earth, and that's when the Rockets' record will come into play.\xa0Houston's climb back into the playoff picture gives Harden the hot hand in the MVP race, but like last year, it will come down to the team's final record.</p>, <p>Through all of the discretionary fog, the MVP ideally goes to the best player on the best team.\xa0By those standards,\xa0Giannis Antetokounmpo of the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/milwaukee-bucks">Milwaukee Bucks</a> (26-10) is the top candidate, followed by Kawhi Leonard of the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/toronto-raptors">Toronto Raptors</a> (28-11).</p>, <p>Harden was an easy choice last season because Houston finished with the best record in the league at 65-17, and his numbers were off the charts.\xa0If he can lead his team to the No. 1 or No. 2 seed in the West by the time the voters have to make their selection, he'll have a legitimate chance at repeating.</p>, <p>Luckily for Harden, there appears to be great parity in the league this year. There is no real dominant team when considering records.</p>, <p>The defending champion Warriors have the fifth-best record in the league, and the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/boston-celtics">Boston Celtics</a> have the eighth-best. Both teams were earmarked as the favorites to make the NBA Finals.\xa0The <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/denver-nuggets">Denver Nuggets</a> and <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/oklahoma-city-thunder">Oklahoma City Thunder</a> are playing surprisingly well, so for now, everything is up for grabs.</p>, <p>Another plus for the Rockets is they seem to have found the right mix of players.</p>, <p>Danuel House is found money, and Austin Rivers looks like a perfect fit for D'Antoni's system.\xa0Houston is averaging 7.9 more made three-pointers than its opponents since the 126-111 win over the <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/los-angeles-lakers">Los Angeles Lakers</a> on Dec. 13 and has out-rebounded opponents in seven of the last 10 games.</p>, <p>The Rockets have also\xa0won close games and have taken a huge step defensively.\xa0They are 24th in defensive efficiency for the year at 111 but are 10th over the last 10 games at <a href="https://stats.nba.com/teams/advanced/?sort=DEF_RATING&amp;dir=-1&amp;CF=MIN*GE*15&amp;Season=2018-19&amp;SeasonType=Regular%20Season&amp;DateFrom=12%2F13%2F2018&amp;DateTo=12%2F31%2F2018" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">107.8</a>.</p>, <p>If CP3 gets healthy and Gordon recaptures his ability to knock down open threes, Houston could be poised to mirror the team that everyone saw last season.\xa0That can only improve Harden's chances at making good on his prediction.</p>, <p>"There's a lot of games left, but if he continues to play at this level, of course there is no debate on who is the MVP," Clint Capela said. "I mean, we all see what he's doing. Everybody sees it. All he has to do is keep playing at this level every single night, and he's the MVP."</p>, <p>\xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0</p>, <p><em>Unless otherwise indicated, all stats courtesy of\xa0<a href="https://www.basketball-reference.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Basketball Reference</a>\xa0or\xa0<a href="http://stats.nba.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">NBA.com</a>.</em></p>, <p><em>Maurice Bobb covers the<span>\xa0</span>NBA<span>\xa0</span>for Bleacher Report. Follow Maurice on Twitter,<span>\xa0</span><a href="https://twitter.com/ReeseReport" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">@ReeseReport</a>.</em></p>]
[<p class="label">\n\t\t\tTrending:\t\t</p>, <p>Don\u2019t tell Chad Reed that he is over the hill because right now he is still having too much fun flying over them. \n<p>Supercross is a brutal, bone-jarring sport, and at 36, riders are usually several pages into the next chapter of their lives, icing their bruises and aching joints. \n<p>But Reed keeps going \u2026 and going. Saturday night at Angel Stadium, Reed will begin his 17th season in the AMA season opener, and he will be the oldest competitor. <div class="s2nFriendlyFrame k k-XOBj4afj" data-type="float"></div><script data-type="s2nScript" src="https://embed.sendtonews.com/player4/embedcode.js?fk=XOBj4afj&amp;cid=8130&amp;floatwidth=400&amp;floatposition=bottom-right" type="text/javascript"></script>\n<p>There are days when he said he can sense his age, feeling \u201cpain in muscles I never knew I had.\u201d \n<p>\u201cBut in some ways I feel better. There are days where it all seems easier. You have a better grasp of understanding what you just did, and take care of yourself then and there,\u201d Reed said. \u201cAnd then that way when you do wake up the next day, it is improved, and you have already started the recovery process. That only comes after spending 20 years in the sport.\u201d \n<p>He\u2019s in much better shape than he was at this point one year ago. When he showed up for the first race in Anaheim last January, he was just beginning to take his first steps after breaking his right ankle a few months earlier. \n<p>He shouldn\u2019t have been up and around at the time, but he needed to get moving if he was going to have any chance to sit on his Husqvarna at Angel Stadium. \n<p>He finished 15th in the main event and went on to ride in all 17 races on the schedule, making his 228th start in Tampa to break Mike LaRocco\u2019s all-time record. \n<p>But his ankle, being held together by a plate and four screws, was a constant issue. <div class="dfp-ad dfp-Cube_Article" data-ad-unit="Cube_Article" id="div-gpt-ad-Cube_Article">\n<script type="text/javascript">\n\t\t\t\t\t\tif ( "undefined" !== typeof googletag ) {\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\tgoogletag.cmd.push( function() { googletag.display("div-gpt-ad-Cube_Article"); } );\n\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\t</script>\n</div>\n<p>\u201cAnd because of that, I wasn\u2019t in shape. I wasn\u2019t healthy,\u201d Reed said. \u201cI never had the fitness. I took a lot of time off in May (after the season ended) to work on range of motion and getting back in shape. That was the most difficult season of my career. This year, I want to put more emphasis on being competitive. I want to be the oldest guy to win a race, I don\u2019t know why but that is important to me.\u201d \n<p>And there\u2019s a good chance this season that Reed could steal another record from LaRocco, who won the 2004 Indianapolis main event when he was 33 years, 1 month and 8 days old. \n<p>Reed is finally back on a factory bike, joining Justin Hill at the Suzuki-backed Joe Gibbs Racing team. Weston Peick was supposed to be at this race for Gibbs. At first glance, Reed said it\u2019s easy to assume that he is filling in for Peick, who suffered severe facial injuries when a bike essentially landed on his face during a race in Paris on Nov. 17. \n<p>But Reed said the goal was to be a third rider on the team. His bike and its parts had a corner of the shop since sometime around August, and he didn\u2019t move into Peick\u2019s place after the crash. \n<p>Reed said he has a contract to keep him on a bike through the Supercross season should Peick happen to make a miraculous recovery. \n<p>\u201cAnd we would love to have that problem,\u201d Reed said. \n<p>But three riders definitely make a full-house in a Supercross where two-bike teams are the norm, and currently JGR is not fully funded, Reed said. His bike and its parts had a corner of the shop since sometime around August, and he didn\u2019t move into Peick\u2019s place after the crash. \n<p>Reed said he has a contract to keep him on a bike through the Supercross season should Peick happen to make a miraculous recovery. \n<p>\u201cAnd we would love to have that problem,\u201d Reed said. \n<p>But three riders definitely make a full-house in a Supercross where two-bike teams are the norm, and currently JGR is not fully funded, Reed said. They have been diving deep into Reed\u2019s little black book from when he owned his own team, hoping to find a sponsor. \n<p>And for Reed, that is not a problem at all. \xa0Chasing corporate dollars was one of the things he enjoyed the most when he ran his own program from the end of 2010 through 2015. \n<p>When he does finally does finally give up riding, he said he\u2019d love to fill that type of role for a team, running he day-to-day operations. \n<p><aside class="related left"><h2 class="widget-title" data-curated-ids="" data-relation-type="automatic-primary-section">Related Articles</h2><ul><li>\n<a class="article-title" href="https://www.ocregister.com/2019/01/03/eli-tomac-starts-quest-for-third-consecutive-supercross-title/" title="Eli Tomac starts quest for third consecutive Supercross title">\n<span class="dfm-title">\n\t\t\tEli Tomac starts quest for third consecutive Supercross title\t\t</span>\n</a>\n</li><li>\n<a class="article-title" href="https://www.ocregister.com/2018/12/27/super-trucks-will-be-a-part-of-grand-prix-of-long-beach-in-years-ahead/" title="Super Trucks will be a part of Grand Prix of Long Beach in years ahead">\n<span class="dfm-title">\n\t\t\tSuper Trucks will be a part of Grand Prix of Long Beach in years ahead\t\t</span>\n</a>\n</li></ul></aside>And he could be ready to make the move in the near future. \n<p>Reed, a 44-time main event winner and two-time series champion, said this could be his last season. \n<p>\u201cBut for me, there is never a plan. They have been diving deep into Reed\u2019s little black book from when he owned his own team, hoping to find a sponsor. \n<p>And for Reed, that is not a problem at all. \xa0Chasing corporate dollars was one of the things he enjoyed the most when he ran his own program from the end of 2010 through 2015. \n<p>When he does finally does finally give up riding, he said he\u2019d love to fill that type of role for a team, running he day-to-day operations. \n<p><aside class="related left"><h2 class="widget-title" data-curated-ids="" data-relation-type="automatic-primary-section">Related Articles</h2><ul><li>\n<a class="article-title" href="https://www.ocregister.com/2019/01/03/eli-tomac-starts-quest-for-third-consecutive-supercross-title/" title="Eli Tomac starts quest for third consecutive Supercross title">\n<span class="dfm-title">\n\t\t\tEli Tomac starts quest for third consecutive Supercross title\t\t</span>\n</a>\n</li><li>\n<a class="article-title" href="https://www.ocregister.com/2018/12/27/super-trucks-will-be-a-part-of-grand-prix-of-long-beach-in-years-ahead/" title="Super Trucks will be a part of Grand Prix of Long Beach in years ahead">\n<span class="dfm-title">\n\t\t\tSuper Trucks will be a part of Grand Prix of Long Beach in years ahead\t\t</span>\n</a>\n</li></ul></aside>And he could be ready to make the move in the near future. \n<p>Reed, a 44-time main event winner and two-time series champion, said this could be his last season. \n<p>\u201cBut for me, there is never a plan. This game has the highest projected over/under of the slate (49). Luck will likely be the highest-owned quarterback, but he\u2019s impossible to fade.</p>, <p>Watson, fantasy\u2019s <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/news/fantasy-football-facts-to-know-for-wild-card-weekend-2018">No. 2 quarterback over the second half of the season</a>, is playing as a home favorite in a game with the highest over/under and best <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/news/fantasy-football-snaps-pace-stats-wild-card-2018">snap pace outlook</a>. Watson pummeled Indy for 375 passing yards and two passing touchdowns along with 41 rushing yards and a rushing touchdown back in Week 4 and put together a respectable (albeit less explosive) performance against them in Week 14. Watson has been on fire, this game has the best floor/ceiling combination of the weekend, and he\u2019s playing in a favorable game environment \u2014 what\u2019s not to like?</p>, <p>Elliott comes in fresh off Dallas\u2019 Week 17 built-in bye to face a Seahawks rush defense that has hemorrhaged 4.6 rushing YPC against on the season and 5.1 YPC against over the second half of the year. Running backs have also hauled in 102 receptions against Seattle this year, fifth-most in the NFL.</p>, <p>Carson finished the season fifth in rushing yards (1,151) and was first in rushing attempts over the final month (90). Dallas\u2019 rush defense was gashed over the final three weeks, giving up 112 rushing yards per game and 1.7 rushing TDs per game. Carson is still relatively cheap compared to how he performed over the second half of the season \u2014 and especially over the final month.</p>, <p>Miller is extremely cheap ($4,900 on DraftKings; $6,400 on FanDuel), and I\u2019m considering him a great play relative to his salary. Miller has over 95 total yards and/or a touchdown in seven of his last eight healthy games, with four 100-yard rushing efforts in that span (important if you\u2019re playing DraftKings). The Colts rush defense is average \u2014 this isn\u2019t a <em>great</em> matchup, but it\u2019s certainly not bad \u2014 and the Texans are slight home favorites in a game with the best scoring potential.</p>, <p>Indianapolis did a good job keeping Hopkins in check in Week 14 \u2014 he had a 4-36-1 (10) line in that game \u2014 but Hopkins shredded them in Week 4 with a 10-169-1 (12) performance. Over the final three games of the season, Hopkins had 31 receptions on 39 targets for 421 yards. You can\u2019t afford to pass up his floor/ceiling combination on such a short slate.</p>, <p>Hilton doesn\u2019t have nearly the same target volume as Hopkins, but he can \u201cget there\u201d with only half as many opportunities. Hilton blasted Houston for 9-199-0 (12) in Week 14 and 4-115-0 (6) in Week 4. In his career, Hilton <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/news/fantasy-football-facts-to-know-for-wild-card-weekend-2018">averages</a> over 100 yards and 0.6 touchdowns per game against Houston.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="alignnone wp-image-274949" sizes="(max-width: 706px) 89vw, (max-width: 767px) 82vw, 740px" src="https://media.profootballfocus.com/2019/01/Allen-Robinson-Targets.png" srcset="https://media.profootballfocus.com/2019/01/Allen-Robinson-Targets.png 1920w, https://media.profootballfocus.com/2019/01/Allen-Robinson-Targets-300x169.png 300w, https://media.profootballfocus.com/2019/01/Allen-Robinson-Targets-768x432.png 768w, https://media.profootballfocus.com/2019/01/Allen-Robinson-Targets-1024x576.png 1024w" width="1920"/></p>, <p>Robinson, one of the league\u2019s leading <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/news/fantasy-football-facts-to-know-for-wild-card-weekend-2018">positive touchdown regression candidates</a>, squares off against a depleted Eagles secondary that has allowed the third-most fantasy points to opposing receivers this season. Robinson has at least seven targets in six of his last seven games.</p>, <p>Ertz has been one of the most bankable fantasy tight ends all season long, and that\u2019s not going to change in the playoffs with only four games on tap. Ertz has shown a volatile floor/ceiling combination over the last three games with <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/nfl/players/nick-foles/7089">Nick Foles</a>, producing just 4.5 PPR points last week after scoring 38 DraftKings points the week before. The big swings make him a viable GPP fade, but I\u2019ll take his <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/news/fantasy-football-facts-to-know-for-wild-card-weekend-2018">record-setting targets</a> in cash.</p>, <p>Ebron is one of the other tight ends we\u2019ve been comfortable playing in 2018, and we should be grateful to have both him and Ertz to choose from this weekend. Ebron has a better on-paper matchup against the Texans, who have allowed the second-most fantasy points to opposing tight ends this season. This year, Ebron averaged nine targets per game against Houston with a touchdown in both games.</p>]
[<p id="iAoMVY">The <a href="http://www.sbnation.com/nfl/teams/indianapolis-colts"><strong>Indianapolis Colts</strong></a> have released their injury report for Wednesday, their second of the week after releasing an estimation of a player\u2019s participation from Tuesday\u2019s walkthrough practice.</p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">Ryan Kelly and Clayton Geathers return to practice: <a href="https://t.co/45XiEvzz97">https://t.co/45XiEvzz97</a> <a href="https://t.co/QHfTh04coM">pic.twitter.com/QHfTh04coM</a></p>, <p id="ZkZuAU">The biggest news of the day was the return of starting center <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/players/276892/ryan-kelly">Ryan Kelly</a> (neck) and safety <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/players/254572/clayton-geathers">Clayton Geathers</a> (knee) to practice, and both were full participants. <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/players/303020/ryan-kelly">Kelly</a> has been nursing his neck injury since getting hurt against the <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/teams/new-york-giants">Giants</a> in Week 16, while <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/players/255660/clayton-geathers">Geathers</a> was hurt in the Colts\u2019 game against the <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/teams/dallas-cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> in Week 15.</p>, <p id="57eFXp">Four Colts \u2014 wide receivers <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/players/16772/ryan-grant">Ryan Grant</a> (toe) and <a href="https://www.sbnation.com/nfl/players/154920/t-y-hilton">T.Y. [<p>\r\n                  Wednesday, Jan 02, 2019 07:04 PM\r\n                </p>, <p>Seahawks.com Reporter</p>, <p>The 2018 season has been a difficult one for Doug Baldwin. Injuries took their toll on the Seahawks receiver, who missed three games and played at something less than 100 percent for pretty much all of the other 13 games.</p>, <p>Baldwin, who had 29 touchdowns in the previous three seasons, didn\u2019t secure his first touchdown pass until Week 11, his reaction to that score after the game being a one word response of, \u201cfinally.\u201d And after piling up 247 catches and 3,188 yards in the previous three seasons and earning Pro-Bowl honors twice, Baldwin was limited to 50 catches for 618 yards and five touchdowns this year.</p>, <p>Baldwin, who missed training camp and the preseason with knee injury, only to hurt his other knee in the regular-season opener, causing him to miss the next two games, has battled knee, groin, hip, elbow and shoulder injuries throughout this season, and he again is on the injury report this week with a knee injury that limited him in Wednesday\u2019s practice.</p>, <p>But despite that designation, Baldwin has been healthier lately than he was for much of the regular season, which has shown in the impact he has made in recent games, most notably his 126-yard game in a Week 16 win over Kansas City that saw him make two of the game\u2019s biggest plays on very high degree-of-difficulty catches. And now that the Seahawks are in the playoffs, Baldwin feels like he can put all the struggles of the regular season behind him and start over relatively healthy and ready to help the Seahawks go on what they hope can be a long playoff run.</p>, <p>\u201cThe biggest thing is the emotional part of it,\u201d he said. \u201cYou feel like you\u2019re in the playoffs so it doesn\u2019t matter what\u2019s thrown at you. You can handle it, and there\u2019s a newness or a refreshing feeling to it because you feel like you\u2019re going into a tournament where anything can happen, and the only thing that really matters is winning, so you put aside everything that you\u2019ve been dealing with in the past subconsciously and you can go for it. I mean, I was talking to our equipment staff yesterday about this. I just feel so much more vibrant. The energy is there because I know it\u2019s playoff time. We look forward to these moments, and I\u2019m not saying that we treat them differently, I\u2019m just saying that there\u2019s a certain energy when you get into the tournament. It\u2019s undeniable.\u201d</p>, <p>As Baldwin noted, the Seahawks aren\u2019t preparing for Saturday\u2019s game against the Cowboys any differently that they would a regular-season game. Seahawks coach Pete Carroll has always preached the importance of treating every game as a championship opportunity, and that doesn\u2019t change whether it\u2019s the first week of the regular season or the Super Bowl, but that doesn\u2019t mean there isn\u2019t a certain buzz in the air come playoff time, even if it doesn\u2019t change preparation this week. And for a player who has battled through a difficult season full of injuries, that extra energy can provide a boost.</p>, <p>\u201cIt\u2019s a refreshing feeling in some ways,\u201d Baldwin said. \u201cAgain, the playoffs, to me, it just starts everything over again. Your mindset starts over again. Everything that\u2019s happened in the past, we\u2019ve put that behind us and we\u2019ve focused on what we can control. It is what it is, in terms of injuries, but it doesn\u2019t matter now. There\u2019s no more excuses. We\u2019ve got to do what we\u2019ve got to do. We\u2019ve got four more games.\u201d</p>, <p>And while players like Baldwin and <a href="https://www.seahawks.com/news/k-j-wright-s-return-bolsters-seahawks-defense-heading-into-playoffs">linebacker K.J. Wright</a> are grateful for this return to the playoffs in part because it represents a fresh start after battling injuries all season, even their teammates who played all 16 games are especially appreciative to be back in the postseason after falling short in 2017. Veterans like Bobby Wagner and Russell Wilson, both members of Seattle\u2019s 2012 draft class, had never missed the playoffs before the Seahawks went 9-7 last year and missed out on a Wild Card berth, while Wright and Baldwin only missed the playoffs as rookies in 2011 prior to last season. Not that those four or other veterans took the playoffs for granted in the past, but having felt the disappointment of last year, getting back in a year later is a special feeling, especially in a season in which a lot of outside observers thought the Seahawks would take a step back, not get better.</p>, <p>\u201cMy whole mindset was to never miss it again,\u201d Wilson said. \u201c\u2026 You always want to have a chance. Whenever you get to December, you want to have a chance to make it. I think that\u2019s kind of always been my thought is give ourselves a great chance to go where we want to go, and that\u2019s to win the whole thing. I think at the end of the day, we\u2019ve been able to do that extremely, extremely well. Even last year when we didn\u2019t make it, we still had a chance, a really, really close chance. Unfortunately, we didn\u2019t make it last year, but every year\u2019s a new year. The great thing about this team is the fact that everybody was telling us we couldn\u2019t. I think that it shows the will of this team. It shows the heart of this team and it shows the mindset of this team to be able to think the way that you want to think and go the places that you want to go.\u201d</p>, <p>Prior to last season, the Seahawks had not only made the playoffs every year since 2012, but won at least one playoff game, meaning they were, at worst, one of the final eight teams standing for five straight seasons, so it\u2019s no wonder that Wagner had a rather blunt assessment of watching football from home at a time of year he was used to playing meaningful games.</p>, <p>\u201cIt sucked,\u201d Wagner said. \u201cIt was terrible. We had made the playoffs my whole time here since I\u2019ve been here, so when you had that time off, you have to\u2014the first couple of weeks, it just kind of felt like a bye week where it\u2019s just like \u2018All right, well other teams are playing and you\u2019re not.\u2019 Then, when you\u2019re starting to work out and get ready for next season and realize the season is still going, it\u2019s a terrible feeling to be done in January, so I\u2019m going to do my best to make sure it never happens again.\u201d</p>, <p>Wright, showing the same connection with Wagner that on the field has made them one of the league\u2019s best linebacker tandems, had a very similar description of missing the postseason.</p>, <p>\u201cThat\u2019s terrible,\u201d Wright said. \u201cThat\u2019s terrible. I\u2019ve always been to the playoffs since I\u2019ve been here. Playoff football, it\u2019s just fun, it\u2019s just so much better\u2026 I\u2019m glad that we\u2019re in it this year, and we\u2019ve got to do something while we\u2019re in it.\u201d</p>, <p>Asked if missing the playoffs made him more appreciative of being back, Wright said, \u201cMost definitely. We came up short last year, we didn\u2019t get it done, and we just got back to the drawing board. We had an interesting offseason, but we found a way to make it happen.\u201d</p>, <p>The Seahawks and Cowboys will meet for the second time in the postseason this Saturday in Dallas. [<p>Count Warriors big man Kevon Looney among those who think Golden State could use another center.</p>, <p>\u201cWe used to have six or seven centers on the roster, so another one won\u2019t hurt,\u201d Looney said after shootaround Thursday morning. \u201cWe\u2019re all different. Whatever Coach and (general manager) Bob (Myers) think we need, we probably need it.</p>, <p>\u201cWith (DeMarcus Cousins) still out, we need some more big bodies. In case one of us gets into foul trouble, we just need someone who\u2019s big, can get some rebounds and match up with some guys. It\u2019ll help.\u201d</p>, <p>Looney\u2019s comments came three days after Myers conceded that \u201c<a href="https://www.sfchronicle.com/warriors/article/Warriors-interested-in-adding-another-center-13500854.php">we\u2019ve got a little bit of a void at the five-spot</a>, which we\u2019ve got to keep an eye on, whether that\u2019s through trade or a buyout.\u201d Head coach Steve Kerr echoed the sentiment, saying, \u201cWe\u2019re anxious to get DeMarcus into the fold. But even then, there\u2019s probably room for one more center.\u201d</p>, <p>With Damian Jones likely done for the season with a pectoral injury, the Warriors are without a prototypical center until the 6-foot-11, 270-pound Cousins returns from a torn left Achilles tendon. The undersized Looney and Jordan Bell, with cameos from power forwards Draymond Green and Jonas Jerebko, are anchoring Golden State inside.</p>, <p>Not surprisingly, the results have been uneven. With no one to match some of the top big men\u2019s size, the Warriors have repeatedly gotten bullied on the offensive glass and in the paint.</p>, <p>But with no serviceable 7-foot centers immediately available, Golden State, which has an open roster spot, is left hoping someone surfaces in the trade or buyout markets. The trade deadline is Feb. 7, and the buyout market effectively ends March 1.</p>, <p>In the meantime, Looney, Bell and others will try hold the Warriors over. Their next big test comes Thursday night against Houston\u2019s Clint Capela. At 6-foot-10, 240 pounds with speed that belies his size, Capela teams with James Harden to form one of the NBA\u2019s most daunting pick-and-roll duos. In 33.8 minutes per game this season, Capela is averaging 17 points on 63.6 percent shooting, 12.5 rebounds and 1.9 blocks.</p>, <p>\u201cI know I\u2019ve gotten kind of used to playing against those types of guys,\u201d Looney said. \u201cIt\u2019s kind of tough. Those guys are real physical, and it\u2019s hard to be physical back sometimes, because you get into foul trouble. That\u2019s kind of frustrating.\u201d</p>, <p>Connor Letourneau is a San Francisco Chronicle staff writer. Email: <a href="mailto:cletourneau@sfchronicle.com">cletourneau@sfchronicle.com</a>. Twitter: <a href="https://twitter.com/Con_Chron">@Con_Chron</a></p>, <p>Connor Letourneau moved to the Golden State Warriors beat in September 2016 after a year covering Cal. Previously, he spent two years covering the Oregon State Beavers for The Oregonian. Letourneau is a University of Maryland alum who has interned for The Baltimore Sun and blogged for The New York Times. A Portland, Ore., native, he is interested in telling the stories that extend beyond the field or court.</p>, <p class="title">About</p>, <p class="title">Contact</p>, <p class="title">Services</p>, <p class="copyright">\xa92019 Hearst</p>]

[<p>A few passing clouds. Low 19F. Winds E at 5 to 10 mph..</p>, <p>A few passing clouds. Low 19F. Winds E at 5 to 10 mph.</p>, <p class="text-center"><small><i class="fas tnt-info-circle"></i> Updated: January 3, 2019 @ 5:25 pm</small></p>, <p>Members of the Weber State Wildcats huddle between plays against Utah Valley on Saturday, Dec. 15, 2018, at the Dee Events Center in Ogden.</p>, <p>Members of the Weber State Wildcats huddle between plays against Utah Valley on Saturday, Dec. 15, 2018, at the Dee Events Center in Ogden.</p>, <p>OGDEN \u2014 It\u2019s said some lessons are only learned the hard way. In basketball, the hardest way would be through a loss but Weber State is hoping it wised up through Saturday\u2019s <a href="https://www.standard.net/sports/weber-state/weber-state-blasts-idaho-in-st-half-scratches-out-win/article_500e1804-0cee-55d4-8ad7-87a1d2a16671.html" target="_blank">93-87 win at Idaho</a> as it prepares for a Big Sky homestand against Northern Arizona and Southern Utah.</p>, <p>With a 52-30 halftime lead, the Wildcats kept that margin through the opening segment of the second half when Brekkott Chapman drove baseline and <a href="https://twitter.com/WeberStateMBB/status/1079877543178584064" target="_blank">dunked over UI\u2019s Scott Blakney</a> for a 60-38 lead.</p>, <p>But Idaho slowly worked back into the game and, when Cameron Tyson drained three tough 3-pointers in the final 1:21, it nearly put the game in doubt. WSU allowed 57 second-half points.</p>, <p>\u201cWhat we did is kind of fooled ourselves into thinking it\u2019s OK to go through the motions,\u201d senior center Zach Braxton said. \u201cThat\u2019s not what Weber State does. We\u2019re not going to do it again. Not this year.\u201d</p>, <p>It was the first time since Dec. 1 that Weber State appeared to take a half of defense off \u2014 a game against BYU in which the Wildcats also gave up 57 second-half points. But in that track meet, WSU scored 66 itself that half and won.</p>, <p>Head coach Randy Rahe credited Idaho for playing well and relaxing out of halftime. But he said Idaho gained confidence through easy looks, leading to tougher made baskets, and the Vandals got rolling.</p>, <p>\u201cA lot had to do with our edge or urgency. We didn\u2019t maintain it. We allowed them to get back in it and make it interesting,\u201d Rahe said.</p>, <p>\u201cIt can\u2019t happen. I told the guys we play to a certain standard around here, that didn\u2019t meet our standard and we can\u2019t see that again.\u201d</p>, <p><strong>NORTHERN ARIZONA (JAN. 3)</strong></p>, <p>Weber State (8-5, 2-0 Big Sky) opens the new year by hosting Northern Arizona (3-9, 1-1), a team trying to break out of a three-season funk.</p>, <p>NAU finished third in the 2014-15 Big Sky and went 23-15 after playing for the CIT title. In the three-plus seasons since, the \u2018Jacks have 22 total wins.</p>, <p>This season hasn\u2019t looked any better, results-wise, but NAU did play eight true road games in its non-conference schedule and Rahe says they look better than the team WSU beat twice by 30-plus points last season.</p>, <p>\u201cThey upgraded their talent,\u201d Rahe said. \u201cI see a team that\u2019s playing with a lot of confidence right now. They played well against Montana State, they played Montana really tough for 35 minutes. They are fast, they are athletic and very, very aggressive.\u201d</p>, <p>Some of those new faces: Carlos Hines (13 points per game) and Bernie Andre (11.5) lead the \u2018Jacks in scoring. NAU has five road losses to teams rated similarly to or worse than Weber State by an average of 14 points per contest.</p>, <p>WSU has won 18 of its last 20 against NAU.</p>, <p><strong>SOUTHERN UTAH (JAN. 5)</strong></p>, <p>Southern Utah (5-6, 0-2) visits the Dee Events Center on Saturday after a rough start to conference play. The Thunderbirds played Montana somewhat well (lost by 13) but were surprisingly blown out by 30 against Montana State.</p>, <p>UNLV transfer and senior Dwayne Morgan averaged 13 points through four games but is out for the season with a shoulder injury. [<p class="entry-meta">\n<span class="entry-author author vcard"><a class="url fn n" href="http://f1i.com/author/phillip" rel="nofollow">Phillip van Osten</a></span>\n<span class="entry-date"><a href="http://en.f1i.com/date/2019/01/03/" rel="nofollow"><time class="published" datetime="2019-01-03T08:18:02+00:00">03/01/2019 at 08:18</time><time class="updated" datetime="2019-01-03T08:44:28+00:00">03/01/2019 at 08:44</time></a></span>\n<!-- <span class="entry-category"><a href="http://f1i.com/category/news" rel="category tag">F1 News, Reports and Results</a>, <a href="http://f1i.com/category/news/williams" rel="category tag">Williams</a></span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class="entry-comments"><span>Comments Off<span class="screen-reader-text"> on Kubica says he'll only be as good as Williams' 2019 car</span></span></span> -->\n</p>, <p>F1 returnee Robert Kubica believes his sensational comeback to Grand Prix racing in 2019 will only be as good as the car Williams will produce.</p>, <p>After a year working as a development driver for the British outfit, a task that validated his physical ability to manhandle an F1 car despite the limitations of his right arm injured in his horrific 2011 rally crash, Kubica earned himself a race seat with Williams.</p>, <p>The 34-year-old has no doubts that he is up to the challenge that awaits him this season, but his overall performance will be highly dependent on the car fielded by a team that has struggled in the past two years in F1.</p>, <p>"It's a difficult task and a very ambitious goal, but I think I'm well known for not taking on things that are light and easy," he told <em>Przeglad Sportowy</em> newspaper.</p>, <p>"Whether it works or how close I am, much will depend on how I feel in the car and what the new car is like. How will it behave? This can greatly simplify or complicate the matter," Kubica said.</p>, <p>From the start to the finish of the 2018 season, Williams' drivers lingered at the tail end of the field, with Lance Stroll and Sergey Sirotkin endlessly struggling with the aero inefficiencies and weaknesses of the FW41.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-313233" height="799" sizes="(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" src="http://f1i.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/08/XPB_953034_1200px.jpg" srcset="http://f1i.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/08/XPB_953034_1200px.jpg 1200w, http://f1i.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/08/XPB_953034_1200px-768x511.jpg 768w, http://f1i.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/08/XPB_953034_1200px-545x363.jpg 545w, http://f1i.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/08/XPB_953034_1200px-1000x666.jpg 1000w" width="1200"/></p>, <p>During testing, Kubica experienced firsthand the car's troubles, saying that dealing with its flaws was like "dancing with a partner who cannot dance".</p>, <p>"If a car does not perform as the driver expects, it is not even so much about the speed and the lap times, but the feeling that it gives that can hinder the driver," he added.</p>, <p><strong><u><a href="http://en.f1i.com/gallery/274524-gallery-f1-drivers-wives-and-girlfriends.html">Gallery: The beautiful wives and girlfriends of F1 drivers</a></u></strong></p>, <p><em>Keep up to date with all the F1 news via <strong><u><a href="https://www.facebook.com/F1icom">Facebook</a></u></strong> and <strong><u><a href="https://twitter.com/F1icom">Twitter</a></u></strong></em></p>, <p></p>, <p>Keep informed with the latest F1 news, reports and results from F1i.com. Also bringing you live reporting, features, interviews, videos, pictures and classic content.</p>]
[<p><strong>Published:</strong> <time class="entry-date published pubdate" datetime="2019-01-02T19:24:16+00:00" itemprop="datePublished">January 2, 2019</time> </p>, <p><strong>Updated:</strong> <time class="updated" datetime="2019-01-02T19:24:16+00:00" itemprop="dateModified">January 2, 2019 7:24 PM CST</time> </p>, <p class="filed_under"><strong>Filed Under:</strong></p>, <p>DETROIT \u2014\xa0Johnny Gaudreau can\u2019t miss.</p>, <p>He couldn\u2019t miss \u2014 at least it seemed that way \u2014 during the month of December, stuffing his stocking with 26 points en route to a nod as one of the NHL\u2019s Three Stars of the Month.</p>, <p>And the Calgary Flames\u2019 highlight-machine still hasn\u2019t missed out on an invite to the annual get-together for the best of the best. The 25-year-old left-winger was picked once again Wednesday to represent the Pacific Division at the 2018 NHL All-Star Game, marking his fifth consecutive call to the mid-season showcase.</p>, <p>\u201cEveryone sees his skill and you see how dynamic he is, but if you haven\u2019t coached him, you don\u2019t know how competitive he is and how passionate he is,\u201d praised Bill Peters, an admirer from afar before being hired as Flames bench boss this past summer. \u201cThose are the things that stick out for me that you weren\u2019t aware of, because you have to be around him every day to see it. It burns bright, and it\u2019s each and every day.\u201d</p>, <p>There was all sorts of good news Wednesday for Gaudreau.</p>, <p>Shortly after morning skate at Little Caesars Arena, he was named the NHL\u2019s second star of the month. Just before puck-drop, he officially booked his trip to the NHL\u2019s all-star shindig in San Jose.</p>, <p>Neither comes as any sort of surprise. (The stumper is that Flames captain Mark Giordano, an early frontrunner for the Norris Trophy, isn\u2019t on the initial roster for the Pacific Division, although he is an option on\xa0the\xa0\u2018Last Man In\u2019\xa0fan vote.)</p>, <p>Gaudreau racked up 11 goals and 15 assists in 14 outings during a dazzling December.</p>, <p>Only Tampa Bay Lightning stud Nikita Kucherov, a no-brainer for top honours after the first 30-point month in the NHL since March of 2001, did more scoresheet damage as Santa was loading his sleigh and then digesting all those cookies.</p>, <p>Only Kucherov\u2019s teammate, Steven Stamkos, tickled more twine than Gaudreau over that same span.</p>, <p>For Gaudreau, 26 points on the same calendar page is a new career-best. His December to remember included nine multiple-point performances, one hat-trick and an impressive plus-15 rating.</p>, <p>Johnny Hockey\u2019s first-line pals, centre Sean Monahan and right-winger Elias Lindholm, also enjoyed the most productive months of their respective careers.</p>, <p>\u201cMony and Lindy have been playing really well \u2014 we\u2019ve been <a href="https://calgarysun.com/sports/hockey/nhl/calgary-flames/flames-top-line-up-there-with-the-best-in-nhl">getting some good chemistry together</a>, so it\u2019s been a lot of fun playing with those guys,\u201d Gaudreau said after the morning prep in Detroit. \u201cAnd when I\u2019ve been getting my chances, they\u2019ve been going in. So that has been nice, too.</p>, <p>\u201cPart of my role on this team is creating offence and when I\u2019m not doing that, I feel like I\u2019m letting the team down. You have to come out every night trying to create that offence and our whole line, I think, believes that we can do that night-in and night-out. It doesn\u2019t matter who we\u2019re playing against.</p>, <p>\u201cWe had a good month there. Obviously there are ups and downs throughout a season, but hopefully we can keep this thing going.\u201d</p>, <p>\n<span class="img-caption">\nCalgary Flames Johnny Gaudreau celebrates with the purple Gatorade with teammates Sean Monahan and Elias Lindholm after scoring a power play goal against the San Jose Sharks at the Scotiabank Saddledome on Monday, Dec. 31, 2018.</span>\n<span class="img-author">\n<span itemprop="creator">Al Charest/Postmedia</span></span>\n</p>, <p>Gaudreau arrived in Detroit \u2014 the first stop on a four-game roadie, the midway point on the 82-game regular-season slate \u2014 with 21 tallies and 34 assists already.</p>, <p>The last time a Flames\u2019 skater sizzled to 55 points in the first 40 games of a campaign? That would be way back in 1992-93, when Gary Roberts achieved the feat.</p>, <p>\u201cHe\u2019s right up there with the best playmakers, if not <em>The Best</em>, in our opinion,\u201d said Giordano of Gaudreau. \u201cHe sees the game extremely well, two or three steps ahead of most of us. He\u2019s just been great this year, all year. Dynamic. He\u2019s one of those guys that every time he gets into the offensive zone, it feels like something is going to happen.\u201d</p>, <p>That, Peters has learned, is not just because of Gaudreau\u2019s creativity or sky-high skill level.</p>, <p>Competitiveness is a key ingredient, too.</p>, <p>\u201cEvery night, it\u2019s on display in some regard,\u201d Peters said. \u201cIt\u2019s not easy to be his size and go in and win those battles that he does. And he wins them in different fashion. He wins them with hockey sense. He wins them by being quick. He out-thinks his opponent \u2026 \u201d</p>, <p>The coach continued, referencing Gaudreau\u2019s sensational setup on Lindholm\u2019s strike against the San Jose Sharks on New Year\u2019s Eve, when No. 13 slammed on his brakes and plattered a cross-seam feed as his linemate cruised into the slot.</p>, <p>\u201cIt\u2019s a two-on-two, and he makes a world-class pass that ends up with a guy receiving it right in the wheelhouse with an empty net, and the goaltender has to go east-west,\u201d Peters marvelled. \u201cThat\u2019s a hell of a pass.\u201d</p>, <p>A hell of a player, too.</p>, <p>Off to the all-star weekend again, and deservedly so.</p>, <p><a href="mailto:wgilbertson@postmedia.com">wgilbertson@postmedia.com</a></p>, <p><a href="https://twitter.com/wesgilbertson">Twitter.com/WesGilbertson</a></p>, <p>Stories, pictures and tributes to life. [<p>Trainer Lloyd Kennewell is to close his Adelaide stable and move all his horses to Melbourne in light of prize money cuts in South Australia.</p>, <p>Trainer Lloyd Kennewell is closing his Adelaide stable and moving to Melbourne.<cite><span class="ojLwA">Credit:</span>AAP</cite></p>, <p>Kennewell opened a stable at Caulfield last year and had planned to maintain a presence at Morphettville.</p>, <p>But on Thursday he issued a media statement saying it was not sustainable and he would concentrate solely on Caulfield.</p>, <p>Last month Thoroughbred Racing South Australia announced funding and prize money cuts, citing the state government's failure to return money from the new point of consumption tax to the racing industry.</p>, <p>"There is some very disappointing news coming out of Adelaide in regards to the funding and prize money cuts that the Government have made," Kennewell said.</p>, <p>"We are already well below the prize money levels compared to the eastern states, and our costs are not much different which really hurts the industry.</p>, <p>"It is very sad to see this happen in such a historic state of racing and there is no doubt the future of racing in the state is in turmoil.</p>, <p>"With a heavy heart this has left me with no choice but to speed up my decision to close the Morphettville operation down which will be effective from the end of January, 2019."</p>, <p>Kennewell will move into a renovated 30-horse barn at Caulfield at the beginning of next month.</p>, <p>Phillip Stokes, a dual Adelaide premiership winner, has recently opened a stable at Pakenham in Victoria.</p>, <p><strong>AAP</strong></p>, <p>Copyright \xa9 <!-- -->2019</p>]
