[<p>The 2019 NASCAR season is now within view as we have entered the month of January.</p>, <p>That means a lot of highly anticipated changes in the sport will be visible on track.</p>, <p>Before we get to what to expect from each team specifically, here\u2019s what Cup teams will be dealing with in 2019.</p>, <p>Inspired by what was used in the 2018 All-Star Race, <a class="link rapid-noclick-resp" data-ylk="slk:the new rules package will feature a tapered spacer" href="https://nascar.nbcsports.com/2018/10/02/nascar-announces-2019-rules-package-for-cup/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">the new rules package will feature a tapered spacer</a> to control the engines instead of a restrictor plate. Teams\xa0will have 550 horsepower at tracks 1.33 miles and larger and 750 horsepower at tracks shorter than 1.33 miles.</p>, <p>Some crew chiefs, including Cole Pearn, have said the new package could result in racing that resembles what is seen in the Gander Outdoors Truck Series.</p>, <p><strong>Teams</strong></p>, <p>One team that will not be present this year is Furniture Row Racing, which ceased operations on its No. 78 Toyota after 2018 due to a lack of sponsorship.</p>, <p>Stewart-Haas Racing has yet to announce who will drive its No. 41 Ford this year.</p>, <p>Rick Ware Racing will field two cars with two charters. It has not announced drivers for either car.</p>, <p>Spire Sports + Entertainment will field the No. 77 with a charter purchased from Furniture Row Racing. [<p>Now that the holidays are officially in the rearview mirror, we can say baseball will be played \u201cthis year\u201d instead of \u201cnext year.\u201d</p>, <p>That\u2019s exciting stuff, but it\u2019s likely not as exciting for the incredible number of big leaguers still looking to score contracts for 2019 and (potentially) beyond. It feels as though there\u2019s been a little more action this winter when compared to last offseason\u2019s snail pace, but a ton of top free agents remain unemployed in January.</p>, <p>Where will they eventually land?</p>, <p>Here we take a look at potential landing spots for 10 top free agents, along with trying to pinpoint the best fit(s) for them.<a href="https://thesportsdaily.com/2019/01/03/mlb-free-agency-evaluating-landing-spots-for-mlbs-remaining-top-free-agents-cmb11/2/"></a></p>, <p><strong><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/h/harpebr03.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Bryce Harper</a></strong></p>, <p>Suitors: Los Angeles Dodgers, Washington Nationals, Philadelphia Phillies, Chicago White Sox, Chicago Cubs</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>We\u2019ve already gone in depth on Harper\u2019s <a href="https://thesportsdaily.com/2018/11/21/evaluating-some-of-bryce-harpers-potential-free-agent-landing-spots-cmb11/" target="_blank">potential market</a>, but some things have changed since then. For instance, the Nationals have <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/sports/2019/01/02/rumors-swirl-bryce-harpers-market-remains-far-blurrier-than-manny-machados/?noredirect=on&amp;utm_term=.3e92c39055cc" target="_blank">reportedly had a number of meetings</a> with their former outfielder and agent Scott Boras. Let\u2019s also not forget that the Dodgers have cleared some payroll (and an outfield roster spot) by trading away <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/p/puigya01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Yasiel Puig</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/k/kempma01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Matt Kemp</a>.</p>, <p>You can never count out Washington based off the team's history and how Boras has dealt directly with ownership. However, it\u2019s hard to think the Dodgers aren\u2019t going to try and make a push for the former NL MVP, despite their reported desire for a right-handed impact hitter. Then, of course, there\u2019s always the Phillies, who have money burning in their pocket and are going to have a <a href="https://sports.yahoo.com/report-phillies-face-face-meeting-bryce-harper-194519218.html" target="_blank">face-to-face meeting</a> with Harper soon.</p>, <p>At this point, it seems most likely that Philly will land him based on the circumstances, but anything can happen.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/m/machama01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Manny Machado</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: New York Yankees, Chicago White Sox, Philadelphia Phillies</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>Similar to Harper \u2014 and a number of other top free agents we\u2019ll talk about \u2014 <a href="https://thesportsdaily.com/2018/11/27/mlb-hot-stove-evaluating-manny-machados-potential-free-agent-landing-spots-cmb11/" target="_blank">we previously went into detail</a> with regard to Machado\u2019s potential suitors. Since then, the infielder\u2019s known market has seemingly been focused around the three above teams he visited following the Winter Meetings.</p>, <p>Despite being on the verge of officially signing <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/t/tulowtr01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Troy Tulowitzki</a> and probably <a href="https://twitter.com/martinonyc/status/1080590702495649792" target="_blank">not offering Machado the most money</a>, the Yankees still appear to be the front-runner.</p>, <p>New York is clearly preparing for a scenario where Machado doesn\u2019t choose it, and if he does, it gives the Yankees plenty of options while <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/g/gregodi01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Didi Gregorius</a> is on the disabled list \u2014 including floating <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/a/andujmi01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Miguel Andujar</a> in trade talks.</p>, <p>The Phillies are <a href="https://twitter.com/BNightengale/status/1080895263470829569" target="_blank">expected to be the highest bidder</a> for both Harper and Machado, so we\u2019ll see how everything plays out soon enough.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/k/keuchda01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Dallas Keuchel</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: Cincinnati Reds, Philadelphia Phillies, Los Angeles Angels, Milwaukee Brewers, Texas Rangers, Houston Astros</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>You\u2019ll be shocked to know that we\u2019ve also looked at Keuchel\u2019s <a href="https://thesportsdaily.com/2018/12/19/dallas-keuchel-rumors-evaluating-free-agent-landing-spots-cmb11/" target="_blank">possible landing spots</a>. However, things may start to pick up since the southpaw now appears to be the best available starter left on the market.</p>, <p>The Reds just feel like such a perfect fit. They\u2019re tired of losing and have been aggressive with regard to making offseason upgrades. Even with <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/w/woodal02.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Alex Wood</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/r/roarkta01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Tanner Roark</a> now in the rotation, they still have a number of question marks. <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/search/search.fcgi?pid=castilu02,castilu01,castil014lui,castil018lui,castil015lui&amp;search=Luis+Castillo&amp;utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Luis Castillo</a> had an up-and-down sophomore campaign, <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/d/desclan01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Anthony DeSclafani</a>\n<a href="https://thesportsdaily.com/2019/01/01/fantasy-baseball-six-mlb-starting-pitchers-with-a-lot-to-prove-in-2019-cmb11/5/" target="_blank">has a lot to prove</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/m/mahlety01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Tyler Mahle</a> has struggled with his command through his first 132 big-league innings.</p>, <p>While it\u2019d also be intriguing to see the Brewers make a serious pursuit, that might only happen if the Boras client\u2019s asking price lowers. For a team that was just one win away from the World Series this past October, the Brewers also have a number of varying rotation question marks. Between <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/n/nelsoji02.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Jimmy Nelson</a>, <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/w/woodrbr01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Brandon Woodruff</a>, <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/a/anderch01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Chase Anderson</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/d/davieza02.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Zach Davies</a>, Milwaukee could use a little certainty. Keuchel can provide that \u2014 he\u2019s tossed 200-plus innings three times since 2014 and has accumulated fewer than 150 frames in a season once since becoming a full-time big-league starter in 2013.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/k/kimbrcr01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Craig Kimbrel</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: Atlanta Braves, Boston Red Sox</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>Yes, we also looked at Craig Kimbrel\u2019s <a href="https://thesportsdaily.com/2018/12/04/mlb-free-agency-evaluating-craig-kimbrels-landing-spots-cmb11/" target="_blank">possible landing spots</a> in a more in-depth post, but this is the last one, we promise. While it\u2019s clear to see which teams could use a reliever of his caliber, his record-breaking asking price is what\u2019s really holding up his market.</p>, <p>That\u2019s what happens when you\u2019re looking for a six-year guarantee around $100 million.</p>, <p>The Phillies made sense due to their ability to spend, but they may no longer be interested after agreeing to a two-year, $23 million deal with <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/r/roberda08.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">David Robertson</a>. The Cardinals were a speculative fit earlier in the winter, but they also pivoted to <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/search/search.fcgi?pid=millean01,miller014and,miller011and&amp;search=Andrew+Miller&amp;utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Andrew Miller</a>.</p>, <p>Kimbrel\u2019s best bet may be lowering his asking price significantly and going back to the Red Sox. Without a real clear market and sky-high contract demands, this could become a wait-and-see situation that feels a lot like the <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/m/martijd02.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">J.D. Martinez</a> situation from last winter.</p>, <p>Boston was interested in Robertson but didn\u2019t bite on the guarantee he received from Philly. It\u2019ll be interesting to see how long Kimbrel has to wait for a deal to materialize and how far below his original asking price it seems like he\u2019ll fall.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/g/grandya01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Yasmani Grandal</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: Los Angeles Dodgers, Cleveland Indians, Oakland Athletics, Chicago White Sox, Houston Astros</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>Yasmani Grandal\u2019s market has taken some time to crystallize because of the non-stop <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/r/realmjt01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">J.T. Realmuto</a> rumors. Despite the Miami Marlins\u2019 high asking price, he\u2019s clearly the crown jewel when it comes to catcher acquisitions based on how things have played out thus far.</p>, <p>As for Grandal\u2019s immediate future, a number of the teams currently connected to him don\u2019t make sense unless his contract demands crater. The Indians have been slashing payroll while trying to stay competitive, so that\u2019s not a fit at a multi-year guarantee. The A\u2019s probably won\u2019t be filling their catching need at the top of the market, either. Heck, they just lost <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/l/lucrojo01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Jonathan Lucroy</a> via free agency, who signed for less than $4 million with the Angels.</p>, <p>The Astros have <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/c/chiriro01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Robinson Chirinos</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/s/stassma01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Max Stassi</a> on their roster, but that hasn\u2019t stopped them from pursuing Realmuto. And Grandal\u2019s most recent employer, the Dodgers, aren\u2019t interested in re-signing him for more than one year.</p>, <p>That leaves the White Sox, who have a ton of financial flexibility, are interested in making progress in their rebuild, and have made subtle upgrades by acquiring <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/n/novaiv01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Ivan Nova</a>, <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/a/alonsyo01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Yonder Alonso</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/c/colomal01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Alex Colome</a>. They\u2019ve also signed <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/m/mccanja02.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">James McCann</a> to pair with <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/c/castiwe01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Welington Castillo</a> behind the plate, but neither is a huge financial burden if they decide to switch gears.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/p/polloaj01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>A.J. Pollock</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: New York Mets, Cincinnati Reds, Chicago White Sox, Atlanta Braves</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?\xa0</p>, <p>This is another situation that\u2019s a bit cloudy because of both Pollock\u2019s asking price (around five years and $80 million), along with being behind the big domino (Harper) that needs to fall first.</p>, <p>The Reds still need a center fielder after non-tendering <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/search/search.fcgi?pid=hamilbi02,hamilbi01&amp;search=Billy+Hamilton&amp;utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Billy Hamilton</a>, but they\u2019ve already invested a lot of money into the outfield with the acquisitions of Puig and Kemp. The Mets look like the most logical fit based on need since <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/c/cespeyo01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Yoenis Cespedes</a>\u2018 health is up in the air and the only natural center fielder on the 40-man roster being <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/l/lagarju01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Juan Lagares</a>.</p>, <p>While the Mets were sincerely interested in Pollock (and probably still are), a pairing here probably will happen unless the oft-injured 31-year-old eases on his contract demands. If not, there\u2019s space on the roster and in the payroll for him with the White Sox.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/g/gonzama01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Marwin Gonzalez</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: Washington Nationals, San Diego Padres, Los Angeles Angels, New York Mets, basically any contender</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>Trying to pin down Gonzalez\u2019s market is also tough, but that\u2019s because \u201cSwiss G\u201d could fit on just about any club\u2019s roster. He\u2019d be an interesting fit in San Diego, as he could hold shortstop warm for <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/register/player.fcgi?id=tatis-003fer" target="_blank">Fernando Tatis Jr.</a> and then move elsewhere when he gets promoted, but it\u2019s hard to shake off the Nats here.</p>, <p>Washington surely has no problem spending money, and the Nats have a need at second base. However, it\u2019s reported that their preference is to <a href="https://theathletic.com/736074/2018/12/31/the-9-pressing-questions-for-the-nationals/" target="_blank">find a solution</a> on a short-term deal so prospect <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/register/player.fcgi?id=kieboo000car&amp;utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Carter Kieboom</a> isn\u2019t blocked. Gonzalez, a Boras client, will definitely get a multi-year guarantee, so one might imagine heading to D.C. is out of the cards.</p>, <p>But maybe not. Gonzalez could play second base in 2019, and if the Nats can\u2019t retain third baseman <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/r/rendoan01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Anthony Rendon</a> (another Boras client), Marwin could shift over to the hot corner. Or, he could slide over to first base since <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/search/search.fcgi?pid=zimmery01,zimmer006rya,zimmer004rya&amp;search=Ryan+Zimmerman&amp;utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Ryan Zimmerman</a> is approaching the final year of his current contract.</p>, <p>Versatility with the glove is a wonderful thing.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/b/brittza01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Zach Britton</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: New York Yankees, Boston Red Sox</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>With Robertson finding a home in Philly, Britton may now <a href="https://twitter.com/JeffPassan/status/1080894191469768704?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed&amp;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.mlb.com%2Fnews%2Fzach-britton-rumors%2Fc-301737818" target="_blank">be the next top reliever</a> to sign a contract. He hasn\u2019t re-created the dominant two-year stretch he had with the Baltimore Orioles from 2015-16 (1.22 ERA, 0.91 WHIP, 30.2 percent strikeout rate, 6.2 percent walk rate and 83 saves in 132.2 innings), but he\u2019s still a solid and proven veteran option for the back end of any bullpen.</p>, <p>With the Phillies likely out of the picture, this could come down to being a good, old-fashioned fight between the Red Sox and Yankees. Although Boston might be more interested in waiting out Kimbrel, it could offer Britton an opportunity to close again. <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/c/chapmar01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Aroldis Chapman</a>\u2018s presence doesn\u2019t give the Yankees the luxury of offering that, but Britton has already mentioned he\u2019d take a <a href="https://www.nj.com/yankees/2018/10/zach_britton_why_im_open_to_lesser_role_re-signing.html" target="_blank">lesser bullpen role</a> to return to the Bronx.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/o/ottavad01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Adam Ottavino</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: New York Yankees, Boston Red Sox, Chicago White Sox, Colorado Rockies</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>Ottavino picked the perfect time to have a career year. He posted personal bests in ERA (2.43), hard-hit rate allowed (25.3 percent), strikeout rate (36.3 percent) and fWAR (2.0) while drastically cutting down his homers allowed per nine innings (0.58) in 77.2 innings for the Rockies last season.</p>, <p>Colorado is open to retaining him, but it's already invested a ton into <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/d/daviswa01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Wade Davis</a>, <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/m/mcgeeja01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Jake McGee</a> and <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/s/shawbr01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Bryan Shaw</a>. So who knows how much more flexibility the Rockies have to invest in the bullpen moving forward.</p>, <p>There\u2019s a fair amount of overlap in potential suitors for Britton and Ottavino, and for good reason. It\u2019s likely that their eventual landing spots may depend on who signs first. The wild card here could be the White Sox, as they have plenty of space in the payroll to outbid others if they really want to acquire the 33-year-old right-hander to pair with Colome.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/l/lowrije01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank"><strong>Jed Lowrie</strong></a></p>, <p>Suitors: Washington Nationals, Milwaukee Brewers, Colorado Rockies, Boston Red Sox</p>, <p>Best fit(s)?</p>, <p>Lowrie has put together consecutive stellar (and nearly identical) campaigns with the Oakland A\u2019s after struggling in 2016. What\u2019s tricky for the veteran second baseman is that he\u2019s looking for a multi-year commitment as he enters his age-35 season.</p>, <p>The Nats and Brewers would both be interesting fits because they\u2019re likely contenders with openings at second base. At this point in the winter, it\u2019s possible Lowrie would eventually settle for a two-year deal, allowing Washington and Milwaukee to not block their respective up-and-coming second-base prospects.</p>, <p>How fun would it be for the Rockies to make a splash here, though? Their offense has struggled mightily over the past two years, and they just made a significant upgrade by signing <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/m/murphda08.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Daniel Murphy</a> for two years. He\u2019ll slide into first base, still leaving second open due to <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/l/lemahdj01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">DJ LeMahieu</a>\u2018s free agency. With <a href="https://www.baseball-reference.com/players/a/arenano01.shtml?utm_campaign=Linker&amp;utm_source=direct&amp;utm_medium=linker-" target="_blank">Nolan Arenado</a>\u2018s long-term future up in the air, now is the time to make a run at a long trip into October.</p>, <p>This article first appeared on <a href="http://thesportsdaily.com/" target="_blank">The Sports Daily</a> and was syndicated with permission.</p>, <p>\n\t\t\t\t\t\tYou'll \n\t\t\t\t\t\treceive Yardbarker's daily Top 10, featuring the best sports stories from around the web. \n\t\t\t\t\t\tCustomize your newsletter to get articles on your favorite sports and teams.\n\t\t\t\t\t</p>, <p>Emailed daily. [<p>GLENDALE, AZ - DECEMBER 18: Arizona Coyotes center Clayton Keller (9) looks to pass during the NHL hockey game between the New York Islanders and the Arizona Coyotes on December 18, 2018 at Gila River Arena in Glendale, Arizona. (Photo by Kevin Abele/Icon Sportswire via Getty Images)</p>, <p class="speakable-content">The <a href="http://www.howlinhockey.com">Arizona Coyotes</a> first round (7th overall) selection in 2016 has been formidable since entering the league, having one of the best rookie seasons in recent history.</p>, <p class="speakable-content">In a full 82-game season in 2017/18, <a href="https://www.hockey-reference.com/players/k/kellecl01.html" ref="nofollow">Keller</a> registered 23 goals and 65 total points \u2013 earning himself a place as Calder Cup finalist.</p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">Hey now, he\u2019s an All-Star. \u2b50\ufe0f</p>, <p>Congrats to <a href="https://twitter.com/ClaytonKeller37?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@ClaytonKeller37</a> on his first <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/NHLAllStar?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#NHLAllStar</a> nomination!</p>, <p>\u2192 <a href="https://t.co/X1hhJ6XEpe">https://t.co/X1hhJ6XEpe</a> <a href="https://t.co/kyHTMhKwH4">pic.twitter.com/kyHTMhKwH4</a></p>, <p>\u2014 Arizona Coyotes (@ArizonaCoyotes) <a href="https://twitter.com/ArizonaCoyotes/status/1080608668154945536?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">January 2, 2019</a></p>, <p>This season has seen him continue to score just over 0.75 points per game, an impressive rate for a 20-year-old.</p>, <p>In 40 games this season, Keller has 29 points (eight goals, 21 assists) and leads the Coyotes in total points scored, seven more than second-placed Oliver Ekman-Larsson.</p>, <p>Keller has 96 total points since making his debut with the Coyotes back in the 2016/17 season, where he earned two assists in a three-game stint.</p>, <p>Per <a href="http://arizonasports.com/story/1789555/arizona-coyotes-clayton-keller-selected-to-2019-nhl-all-star-game/">Arizona Sports 98.7FM</a>, Keller\u2019s current points total is the most by any Arizona Coyotes player before the age of 21 \u2013 which the American won\u2019t turn until July this year.</p>, <p>Since the franchise relocated to Arizona ahead of the 1996/97 season, there have only been 24 total All-Stars, with Keller being the latest.</p>, <p>The young forward\u2019s strong performances since becoming a professional has been one of the brightest sparks on the team, along with some sturdy defensive statistics.</p>, <p>With the team not finding much in the way of offensive production, Keller has remained steady and continues to produce at a high rate \u2013 something the team could certainly do with more of.</p>, <p>Keller has arguably been the franchise\u2019s best draft pick in recent years, with <a href="https://www.hockey-reference.com/players/h/haytoba01.html" ref="nofollow">Barrett Hayton</a> and <a href="https://www.eliteprospects.com/player/284911/pierre-olivier-joseph">Pierre-Oliver Joseph</a> still currently developing in juniors while 2015 first-rounder <a href="https://www.hockey-reference.com/players/s/stromdy01.html" ref="nofollow">Dylan Strome</a> was traded away to the Chicago Blackhawks earlier in the season.</p>, <p>Defenceman <a href="https://www.hockey-reference.com/players/c/chychja01.html" ref="nofollow">Jakob Chychrun</a>, who was selected not long after Keller in 2016, has the potential to develop into a Top-2 defenceman, but injuries have so far hampered his progress with the NHL organisation.</p>, <p>With the team once again having a difficult season with little to celebrate, seeing Keller recognised for his rapid development is something that everyone associated with the organisation can be pleased to see.</p>, <p>The All-Star Game is set to take place at the SAP Center in San Jose on January 26th.</p>, <p><em>What do you think of Keller\u2019s All-Star selection? Are you pleased to see him recognised for his performances? Let us know your thoughts in the comments below!</em></p>, <p>Build your own custom daily newsletter with updates on your favorite teams, sent directly to your inbox.</p>, <p class="privacy" style="color: #1E1E1E">Your privacy is safe with us.
